401 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Kohl


No. 00852 Philadelphia 1988


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


395 Pa. Super. 73; 576 A.2d 1049; 1990 Pa. Super. LEXIS 994


October 23, 1989, Argued  
June 18, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Granted November 14, 1990.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the trial court (Pennsylvania), which convicted him of two counts of homicide by vehicle while under the influence of alcohol, two counts of homicide by vehicle, and two counts of driving while under the influence of alcohol or controlled substance.


OVERVIEW: Defendant lost control of his vehicle and collided with a utility pole. The two passengers in the vehicle were killed. While at the hospital, police officers ordered that a blood sample be taken from defendant. The test showed that defendant was intoxicated. Defendant was convicted of two counts of homicide by vehicle while under the influence of alcohol, two counts of homicide by vehicle, and two counts of driving while under the influence of alcohol or controlled substance. Defendant contended that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress. On appeal, the court vacated defendant's conviction and remanded for a new trial. The blood test was constitutionally invalid because officers did not have probable cause to believe that defendant was driving under the influence of alcohol. Neither the officers nor hospital personnel detected any signs of alcohol consumption by defendant. Defendant did not smell of alcohol and no one observed defendant driving recklessly. There were no alcohol bottles or cups in defendant's vehicle.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for homicide by vehicle, homicide by vehicle while under the influence, and driving while under the influence and remanded for a new trial. Defendant's blood test violated the Fourth Amendment because officers did not have probable cause to believe that defendant was driving while intoxicated.

 

402 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Danforth


No. 01693 Philadelphia 1988


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


395 Pa. Super. 1; 576 A.2d 1013; 1990 Pa. Super. LEXIS 992


October 23, 1989, Argued  
June 14, 1990, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the trial court (Pennsylvania), which convicted defendant of driving under the influence in violation 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 3731(a)(4).


OVERVIEW: A police officer, who did not have probable cause to believe defendant was drunk, asked defendant for a blood sample. Defendant complied with the request, but was not told the test could be used against her. Defendant's motion to suppress was denied based on the implied consent provision of the Motor Vehicle Code, 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 1547(a)(2). The court reversed and remanded defendant's conviction for driving under the influence because the court determined the implied consent provision was unconstitutional under the federal and state constitutions. The implied consent provision violated the Fourth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. IV, because it authorized a search, a blood test, without a requirement of probable cause that a suspect was drunk. Searches authorized pursuant to the implied consent provision violated Pa. Const. art. I, § 8 because the provision did not require any evidence of a crime upon which the blood test could be based. The court could not conclude that defendant voluntarily consented to the blood test because defendant was not put on notice of the possible criminal ramifications of the blood test.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded defendant's conviction for driving under the influence because the blood test administered to defendant was done so without her consent and in violation of her constitutional rights. The implied consent provision for a blood test was unconstitutional under the federal and state constitutions because it allowed a blood test to be taken without probable cause that a crime had been committed.

 

403 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Dranzo v. Winterhalter


Nos. 1280 Pittsburgh, 1989, 1281 Pittsburgh, 1989, 1291 Pittsburgh, 1989, 1282 Pittsburgh, 1989, 1290 Pittsburgh, 1989


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


395 Pa. Super. 578; 577 A.2d 1349; 1990 Pa. Super. LEXIS 999


April 3, 1990, Argued  
June 13, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargument Denied August 13, 1990.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, driver and employer, appealed a decision from the trial court (Pennsylvania) that entered judgment for plaintiffs, mother and daughter, in their personal injury action. Plaintiffs appealed the decision denying their motion for additur.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, mother and daughter, were involved in an automobile accident with defendant driver, while he was working for defendant employer. Plaintiffs initiated a personal injury action against defendants. The trial court entered judgment for plaintiffs. Plaintiffs challenged the award alleging that the trial court abused its discretion denying additur. Defendants contended that the trial court erred in denying their motion for change of venue because plaintiffs' husband and father was employed by the clerk of courts. Defendants also alleged the trial court erred in excluding evidence that plaintiffs were not wearing seat belts. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. The amount of the verdict did not shock the court's conscious, so plaintiffs' additur request was properly denied. Defendants did not offer any evidence or proof that the relationship between plaintiffs and an employee of the clerk of courts would prejudice them. Pursuant to 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 4581(e), evidence of plaintiffs' failure to wear seat belts was properly excluded.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of plaintiffs, mother and daughter, because evidence of their failure to wear seat belts was properly excluded and the trial court properly denied defendants', driver and employer, motion to transfer venue. The verdict did not shock the conscience of the court, so plaintiffs were properly denied additur.

 

404 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Simmers v. American Cyanamid Corp.


Nos. 3433 Philadelphia 1988, 3434 Philadelphia 1988, 3566 Philadelphia 1988, 3565 Philadelphia 1988


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


394 Pa. Super. 464; 576 A.2d 376; 1990 Pa. Super. LEXIS 988


October 25, 1989, Argued  
June 12, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected September 14, 1990. Appeal Denied February 22, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Civil at No. 26 June Term, 1987.

Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Civil at No. 1135 February Term, 1987.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated cases, defendant pharmaceutical companies appealed an order from the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), finding that plaintiff wrongful death litigants properly established personal jurisdiction over defendants. Defendants claimed that, as successor corporations, they were not liable for the actions of their predecessor corporation.


OVERVIEW: A corporation sold an x-ray contrast dye that was used at various medical facilities. Defendants corporations, through various mergers and transactions, obtained the corporation's trademark and patent rights and sold the dye. Plaintiff individuals brought wrongful death and survival suits against defendants. The trial court found personal jurisdiction existed. Defendants appealed, claiming that the forum-related actions of the predecessor corporation could not be attributed to them. Defendants claimed that jurisdiction had to be based on the forum-related activity of the defendants themselves. The appellate court affirmed, finding that the long-arm statute was not violated and due process was not offended. The court held that because defendants became the corporate embodiment of the predecessor corporation, defendants were liable as successor corporations for the prior corporation's product line. The court held that because the predecessor corporation purposely directed its product at forum residents, and the litigation arose directly from the drug's manufacturer and distribution, maintenance of the suit in the forum did not offend due process and was constitutionally sound.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment finding that personal jurisdiction over defendant corporations existed in plaintiff wrongful death litigants' suit because defendants were the corporate embodiments of a predecessor corporation. Defendants were liable for the actions of the predecessor corporation and because the corporation directed its drug to forum residents, personal jurisdiction existed.

 

405 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Nesbit


No. 00310 Harrisburg, 1989


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


394 Pa. Super. 287; 575 A.2d 633; 1990 Pa. Super. LEXIS 972


April 3, 1990, Argued  
June 1, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied October 17, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence Entered May 16, 1989, in the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, Criminal Division, at No. 01301 CD 1988.



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, we affirm.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision from the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania), which entered judgment of sentence to pay the costs of prosecution imposed following his conviction of 43 counts of violating the Medicaid Fraud and Abuse Act and 43 counts of violating The Dental Law, 63 P.S. § 120, et seq.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued first that The Dental Law was unconstitutionally vague in its definition of the duties reserved for performance by licensed hygienists. Defendant contended that the language of the statute did not delineate whether the duty of cleaning teeth above and below the gum line was reserved exclusively for a licensed dental hygienist or whether an unlicensed practitioner, for instance, could perform a portion of the hygienist's functions. Defendant also contended that the evidence was insufficient to sustain the verdict of guilty to both The Dental Law violations and to the medicaid fraud charges. On appeal, the court rejected defendant's arguments. The court held that the commonwealth court had upheld the very provision of The Dental Law challenged by appellant in his void-for-vagueness argument. The court also held that the Commonwealth produced sufficient evidence to support the guilty verdicts to violations of both The Dental Law and the medicaid fraud statute. Accordingly, the court affirmed the judgment of sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of sentence of the trial court, which entered judgment of sentence to pay the costs of prosecution imposed following his conviction of 43 counts of medicaid fraud and other related statutory violations. The court held that the commonwealth court had upheld the relevant statutes, and the Commonwealth produced sufficient evidence to support the guilty verdicts.

 

406 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Redmond


Nos. 3296 Philadelphia 1988, 3297 Philadelphia 1988


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


395 Pa. Super. 286; 577 A.2d 547; 1990 Pa. Super. LEXIS 952


August 22, 1989, Argued  
May 21, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargument Denied July 31, 1990. Appeal Dismissed January 10, 1992, Reported at 1992 Pa. LEXIS 13.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Commonwealth sought review of the decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County (Pennsylvania), which entered two orders that the Commonwealth disclose the identity of a confidential informant and precluded a state trooper from testifying as a witness as a result of the trooper's refusal to reveal the informant's identity.


OVERVIEW: Appellee was charged with the murder of an eight-year-old girl. Appellee filed a request for pretrial discovery under Pa. R. Crim. P. 305 for the name of the confidential informant, referred to in the state trooper's investigation report, who provided the state trooper with information concerning the chief of police, who was a suspect. The state trooper refused to disclose the confidential informant's identity. The lower court issued orders that appellant reveal the identity of informant and precluded the state trooper from testifying as to any aspect of the case. On appeal, the court determined that the disclosure of the informant's identity was relevant, would be helpful to appellee in the preparation of his defense, and was essential to a fair determination of the cause. The failure of the state trooper to disclose the informant was a failure of justice and a prejudice to appellee because it prevented him from preparing a viable defense. Accordingly, the court quashed the appeal and affirmed the lower court's orders.


OUTCOME: The court quashed the appeal and affirmed the lower court's orders requiring that the Commonwealth disclose the identity of a confidential informant and precluding a state trooper from testifying as a witness because the failure of the state trooper to disclose the informant was an injustice and a prejudice to appellee because it prevented him from preparing a viable defense.

Commonwealth v. Williams


No. 02299 Philadelphia 1989


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


394 Pa. Super. 90; 574 A.2d 1161; 1990 Pa. Super. LEXIS 945


March 14, 1990, Argued  
May 17, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of August 7, 1989, in the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County, Criminal Division, at No. 3571/1988.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County (Pennsylvania), which convicted him of loitering and prowling under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 5503 (1983), disorderly conduct under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 5506 (1983), and open lewdness under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 5901 (1983).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with attempted auto theft, open lewdness, disorderly conduct, and loitering and prowling when police observed appellant crouching down on the passenger side of a car wearing only a t-shirt and underwear. The trial court acquitted appellant of attempted auto theft and convicted him on the other charges. The court reversed appellant's conviction for open lewdness because appellant did not appear in the nude as was punishable by Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 5901 (1983). The court reversed appellant's conviction for disorderly conduct because his conduct was not hazardous, as prescribed under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 5506 (1983), because he did not create a condition that involved danger or risk. The court affirmed the lower court's conviction of appellant for loitering and prowling because appellant violated 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 5503 (1983) by entering and lurking inside a car owned by an apartment resident.


OUTCOME: The court reversed appellant's conviction for open lewdness because appellant did not appear in the nude. The court reversed appellant's conviction for disorderly conduct because his conduct was not hazardous. The court affirmed the lower court's conviction of appellant for loitering and prowling because appellant entered and lurked inside a car owned by an apartment resident.

 

408 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Buckman


No. 01344 Philadelphia 1989


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


393 Pa. Super. 453; 574 A.2d 697; 1990 Pa. Super. LEXIS 933



May 10, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order docketed on April 25, 1989 in the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County, Criminal Division, at No. 616 Misc. 1987.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County (Pennsylvania), which convicted defendant of violating Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 73, § 1684 (1989) after defendant refused to allow government inspectors to open two bags of pine bark mulch for inspection.


OVERVIEW: Two agents from the Bucks County Department of Weights and Measures (Department) sought to open two of defendant's bags of pine bark mulch for inspection in order to determine whether the weights and measurements listed on the packages were accurate. Defendant refused the inspection because the agents refused to pay for the bags. Defendant was subsequently fined pursuant to Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 73, § 1684. The court vacated defendant's conviction for violation of Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 73, § 1684. Defendant had standing to challenge the constitutionality of the Department's actions. Defendant was personally aggrieved by the conviction for hindering the duties of the inspector. The court held that the search and seizure provisions of the Weights and Measures Act (Act), Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 73, §§ 1662, 1665, under which the agents were operating, were unconstitutional as applied to businesses that were not the subject of close government regulation. The lawn and garden supply business was not a closely regulated business. The effect of the Act was to abolish the warrant requirement as to a vast number of industries that engaged in ordinary commercial activities.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's conviction. Defendant had the right to refuse inspection of his goods because the search and seizure provisions of the Weights and Measures Act were unconstitutional as applied to the lawn and garden supply industry, an industry that was not closely regulated by the government.

Quarry Office Park Assoc. v. Philadelphia Electric Co.


No. 01689 Philadelphia 1989


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


394 Pa. Super. 426; 576 A.2d 358; 1990 Pa. Super. LEXIS 927


January 9, 1990, Argued  
May 8, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargument Denied July 10, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order in the Court of Common Pleas of Chester County, No. 86-09084.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded. Jurisdiction is relinquished.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant electric company sought review of an order from the Court of Common Pleas of Chester County (Pennsylvania), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee developers and held that appellant received a conditional fee interest in property rather than a fee simple absolute when the property was conveyed. The court further held that the railroad company abandoned the rail line when it conveyed the property.


OVERVIEW: Appellee developers brought an action to quiet title with regard to property conveyed from a railroad company to appellant electric company. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of appellee. On appeal, the court reversed the order granting summary judgment and remanded the case for trial. The court determined that the instruments of conveyances were intended to transfer a railroad right of way and not a fee simple interest. The court held that the railroad company only secured a right of way for railroad purposes by virtue of the instruments of conveyance and therefore the only interest it could pass was a railroad right of way. The court found that a jury question existed because a triable factual dispute existed as to whether the railroad company intended to abandon the line and whether it actually abandoned the line. The court concluded that so long as the owner of the right of way, even if a non-railroad, continued to use the line for railroad purposes, the right of way would not be deemed to have been abandoned.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order granting summary judgment in favor of appellee developers and remanded the case for trial. The court held that because all the original railroad company secured by the conveyances was a right of way for railroad purposes, it could only pass a right of way. However so long as appellant electric company continued to use the line for railroad purposes, the right of way would not be deemed to have been abandoned.

Commonwealth v. Boyle


No. 00116 Pittsburgh, 1989


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


394 Pa. Super. 513; 576 A.2d 967; 1990 Pa. Super. LEXIS 924


September 18, 1989, Argued  
May 2, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargument Denied July 16, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, of Crawford County, at No. 571 C.D. 1984.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of sentence is hereby affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the order from the Court of Common Pleas of Crawford County (Pennsylvania), which convicted him on seven counts of failing to file timely Pennsylvania sales tax returns pursuant to 72 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 7268(b).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted on seven counts of failing to file timely Pennsylvania sales tax returns pursuant to 72 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 7268(b). On appeal, defendant contended that the statute was fatally vague, ambiguous, and failed to give adequate notice as to who may be subject to criminal prosecution for violation. Defendant also contended that the statute was not definite or clear on the time when an omission to file a return may expose a taxpayer to criminal prosecution and the statute did not clearly identify persons responsible for filing such a return. The court rejected defendant's contentions, finding that the statute was clear and not unconstitutional. The court noted that the Tax Code defined "persons" to include corporate officers like defendant. Accordingly, the court affirmed the holding of the lower court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the lower court that convicted defendant on seven counts of failing to file timely Pennsylvania sales tax returns. The court held that the statute was not unconstitutional and clearly identified the persons responsible for filing tax returns.

Commonwealth v. Rich


No. 00051 HBG 1989


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


392 Pa. Super. 380; 572 A.2d 1283; 1990 Pa. Super. LEXIS 860


January 17, 1990, Argued  
April 12, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of December 13, 1988 in the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, Criminal Division, at No. 1405 C.D. 1988.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania), which sentenced him for theft by deception, unlawful use of a computer, forgery, and criminal conspiracy.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant contended that the statutory maximum sentences imposed for forgery and criminal conspiracy were an abuse of discretion because they exceeded sentencing guidelines and because the lower court did not provide a contemporaneous statement of the reasons for the deviation. The court agreed with defendant's contentions, finding that at the sentencing hearing, the Commonwealth argued that the lower court would be justified in deviating from the guidelines and imposing a minimum sentence greater than 18 months but the lower court did not advise defendant of the applicable guideline ranges or state the reason for the deviation. The court found that this was a violation of the sentencing statutes. Accordingly, the court vacated the sentences imposed for forgery and criminal conspiracy, and remanded for resentencing on those counts.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's sentence for forgery and conspiracy, but affirmed the sentence for theft by deception and unlawful use of a computer. The court held that because the lower court neither advised defendant of the applicable sentence guideline ranges, nor stated its reasons for deviating from them, it violated statute.

Franklin Chalfont Assoc. v. Kalikow


Nos. 00605 Philadelphia 1989, 00645 Philadelphia 1989


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


392 Pa. Super. 452; 573 A.2d 550; 1990 Pa. Super. LEXIS 854


October 13, 1989, Argued  
April 10, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal From Order Entered Docketed March 1, 1989 In Court of Common Pleas, Civil Division, Bucks County, No. 89-964-17-5.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded. Jurisdiction relinquished.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant homeowners sought an interlocutory appeal of the order from the Court of Common Pleas, Civil Division, Bucks County (Pennsylvania), which granted appellee builder an injunction relating to picketing and the display of signs.


OVERVIEW: Appellant homeowners expressed their displeasure with appellee builder's failure to fix problems with their homes by picketing appellee's sales office and displaying signs criticizing appellee. The lower court granted appellee an injunction relating to picketing and the display of signs. On review, appellants contended that their acts were protected speech. The court agreed with appellants' contentions, finding that the facts appellee alleged, even if true, did not entitle it to injunctive relief since appellants' activities were entitled to protection under Pa. Const. art I, § 7. The court also held that appellants' speech was similarly protected under U.S. Const. amend. I and XIV. The court noted that appellee's business had no privacy interest in premises which were open to the public and to which the business invited and solicited the public. Accordingly, the court reversed the holding of the lower court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the lower court that granted appellee builder an injunction relating to picketing and the display of signs. The court held that appellant homeowners were entitled to picket under both the United States and Pennsylvania constitutions.

Commonwealth v. Patterson


No. 00400 Pittsburgh 1989


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


392 Pa. Super. 331; 572 A.2d 1258; 1990 Pa. Super. LEXIS 863


December 5, 1989, Argued  
April 6, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence Entered February 17, 1989, in the Court of Common Pleas of Erie County, Criminal Division, at No. 1514 of 1988.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Erie County (Pennsylvania), which entered a judgment of sentence of life imprisonment following conviction by a jury for the murder of a 10-year-old girl.


OVERVIEW: The 10-year-old victim and 6-year-old witness were playing near a bridge in their rural neighborhood. The witness stated that a white male, asked them to help him catch minnows. The victim accompanied the man, but the witness declined. The victim's sister and a friend arrived within minutes seeking victim. The witness informed them that she had accompanied a stranger around the bend. The girls tried to find her in the woods without success. They saw a man leave from the bushes. The police were summoned when the victim was not found. The girl was discovered by one of the police officers, with her throat slashed. Appellant was later apprehended and was identified by witnesses. Appellant denied any knowledge of the crime and was released. Appellant was later arrested and the lower court entered a judgment of sentence of life imprisonment following conviction by a jury for the murder of the victim. The court affirmed the lower court's conviction because the lower court unfailingly was fair and impartial. Therefore, there was no abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment of sentence of life imprisonment following conviction by a jury for the murder of a 10-year-old girl because the lower court unfailingly was fair and impartial. Thus, there was no abuse of discretion.

Commonwealth v. Perez


No. 02286 Philadelphia 1989


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


400 Pa. Super. 622; 576 A.2d 1136; 1990 Pa. Super. LEXIS 4153



March 22, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of July 17, 1989 in the Court of Common Pleas of Lancaster County; Criminal No. 2624 of 1988.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Court of Common Pleas of Lancaster County (Pennsylvania), which sentenced him for a term of not less than four years to eight years imprisonment and fined him $ 25,000 pursuant to the mandatory sentencing provisions of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 7508(a)(3)(iii) after defendant pled guilty to delivery of more than 100 grams of cocaine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to delivery of more than 100 grams of cocaine and was sentenced, pursuant to 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 7508(a)(3)(iii), for a term of not less than four years to eight years imprisonment and fined $ 25,000. Defendant challenged the sentence and the fine, contending that the provisions of § 7508(a)(3)(iii) violated the prohibition against cruel and unusual punishment in U.S. Const. amend. VIII. Defendant also argued that § 7508 (a)(3)(iii) violated Pa. Const. art. I, § 13, which prohibited excessive fines. Because defendant's direct constitutional challenges were waived as a result of his failure to raise them in a motion for reconsideration, defendant contended that his trial counsel was ineffective for failing to preserve the issues. The court affirmed, finding that the sentences found in § 7508 (a)(3)(iii) could not be said to be excessive in relation to the sentences for other severe crimes. The court also found that the fine of $ 25,000 was not so great as itself to be confiscatory and beyond the bounds of all reason and justice. Thus, the court found that defendant's counsel was not ineffective for failing to raise the issues.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court, which sentenced defendant for a term of not less than four to eight years and fined him $ 25,000 for delivery of more than 100 grams of cocaine. The court found that the sentence did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment, that the fine was not excessive, and that defendant's trial counsel did not provide ineffective assistance to defendant.

 

415 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Elrod


No. 03352 Philadelphia 1988


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


392 Pa. Super. 274; 572 A.2d 1229; 1990 Pa. Super. LEXIS 530


November 16, 1989, Argued  
March 7, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargument Denied May 2, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal From Judgment of Sentence Docketed October 26, 1988 In the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, Philadelphia County, No. 8801-3201/3203 and 3205.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction for aggravated assault from the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania). Defendant urged that the evidence was insufficient to support his conviction. Defendant also challenged the constitutionality of his sentence, contending that aggravated assault is a lesser included offense of attempted murder and must therefore have a smaller maximum sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant abducted a woman and threatened her at knifepoint. He was interrupted and restrained by a passerby, allowing the victim to call the police. At trial, defendant was convicted of aggravated assault, simple assault, indecent assault, terroristic threats, recklessly endangering another, and possessing the instruments of a crime. On appeal, defendant challenged the sufficiency of the evidence to convict him of aggravated assault. The court held that the fact that defendant did not carry out his threats did not preclude the jury from finding that he had the intent to carry them out. Furthermore, the trial court properly instructed the jury that an attempt to commit serious bodily injury was necessary for a conviction. Finally, defendant contended that aggravated assault is a lesser-included offense of attempted murder. As such, defendant urged that the maximum penalty for aggravated assault was unconstitutional for being double the maximum sentence for attempted murder. Without addressing the substantive issue, the court held that defendant had waived the issue by failing to raise it before the trial court.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for aggravated assault was affirmed. The court held that the jury could properly have found he had the requisite intent despite the fact that he did not actually carry out his threats of violence. And, the court ruled that by failing to raise his challenge to the constitutionality of his sentence before the trial court, defendant had waived the issue on appeal.

 

416 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Hill v. Nationwide Ins. Co.


No. 3534 Philadelphia 1988


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


391 Pa. Super. 184; 570 A.2d 574; 1990 Pa. Super. LEXIS 393


August 16, 1989, Argued  
February 28, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal Denied July 31, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order entered on November 16, 1988, in the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County, Civil Division, at No. 87-5681.



DISPOSITION: The order of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant provider challenged a decision from the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County (Pennsylvania), which allowed a court in equity to hear a cause that involved the Motor Vehicle Financial Responsibility Law (MVFRL). Appellant contended that appellee insured's claim for medical coverage was precluded from being heard in equity by the MVFRL and that the trial court improperly awarded appellee attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: Appellee insured was injured in an automobile accident. Appellant provider paid medical benefits for nearly a year before terminating coverage. Appellee filed a suit in equity to enjoin the termination and compel appellant to pay future medical expenses. Appellant filed a request to transfer the case out of equity as the Motor Vehicle Financial Responsibility Law (MVFRL) controlled the issue. The request was denied and a decree, which ordered appellant to continue paying appellee's outstanding and future medical costs and awarding attorney fees to appellee, was entered. Appellant sought review, contending that the case was improperly heard in equity and that it was error to award attorney fees. The court held that, in order to protect appellee from having to relitigate the issue of medical coverage, equity jurisdiction was properly asserted. Furthermore, the court held that there was nothing in the MVFRL to preclude the application of equitable relief to appellee's claim. Finally, the court held that as there was ample evidence that appellant acted in bad faith when it denied coverage, 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 1716 of the MVFRL provided for the award of attorney fees.


OUTCOME: The decision of the trial court, to hear appellee insured's claim in equity and to award attorney fees to him, was affirmed. The court held that no statutory provision prevented the trial court from hearing insured's claim in equity, which also served to prevent appellee from having to relitigate the issue of provider's liability over and over again. And, the court held that attorney fees were expressly permitted by statute.

In re Estate of Warner


No. 561 Pittsburgh, 1989


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


391 Pa. Super. 124; 570 A.2d 544; 1990 Pa. Super. LEXIS 320


October 13, 1989, Argued  
February 16, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Order of the Court of Common Pleas, Orphans' Court Division, of Allegheny County, No. 1245 of 1985.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother and daughter income beneficiaries challenged the order of the Court of Common Pleas, Orphans' Court Division, of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which granted appellee executor's petition and directed that inheritance tax, administration expenses, repair costs, and other expenses be paid from income of appellee estate.


OVERVIEW: The income of appellee estate's trusts supported appellant wife for her lifetime, and thereafter, appellant daughter for her lifetime. The trusts owned commercial property, which produced lease income. The estate had insufficient funds and owed state inheritance tax, repair costs, administrative costs, including commissions for appellee executor and counsel fees, and real estate taxes. Appellee executor filed a petition to obtain permission to pay inheritance tax, administrative costs, repair costs, and real estate taxes out of appellee estate's income. The trial court granted appellee executor's petition and directed the costs paid from appellee estate's income and appellants as income beneficiaries challenged the order. The court affirmed that the real estate taxes, repairs, and business privilege taxes were payable from income. However, the court reversed and held that the inheritance tax had to be paid out of principal because the testator's will clearly expressed this intention. The court also reversed, remanded, and held that administrative fees had to be apportioned between income and principal under 20 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 8111(b).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the part of the order directing appellee executor to pay inheritance tax out of appellee estate's income and directed that it be paid out of principal because that was the intention of the testator. The court also reversed the direction to pay administration costs and counsel fees out of income and remanded for apportionment between principal and income in compliance with statute. In other respects the order was affirmed.

 

418 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Ross


No. 1178 Philadelphia, 1989


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


391 Pa. Super. 32; 570 A.2d 86; 1990 Pa. Super. LEXIS 310


December 4, 1989, Submitted  
February 12, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal Denied July 10, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Judgments of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, of Philadelphia County, No. 8806, 1468-1472.



DISPOSITION: The judgments of sentence are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), that granted a judgment of sentence following a conviction of robbery, criminal conspiracy, and possession of an instrument of crime, contending that the evidence was insufficient, the offense did not implicate the mandatory sentence provisions of 42 Pa. Cons Stat. § 9713(a), and the statute was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was found guilty of robbery, in violation of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3701(a)(1)(ii), criminal conspiracy in violation of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 903, and possession of an instrument of crime in violation of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 907(a). Appellant was sentenced to imprisonment of not less than five years or more than ten years for robbery and sentenced to concurrent, lesser terms for criminal conspiracy and possession of an instrument of crime. Appellant contended that the evidence was insufficient, the offense did not implicate the mandatory sentence provisions of 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9713(a), and the statute was unconstitutional because it violated due process and equal protection guarantees and the constitutional proscription against cruel and unusual punishment. The appellate court affirmed the judgments of sentence. The court found that the evidence was sufficient to show that appellant, by use of an unpraised knife, threatened his victim with serious bodily injury. The court held that appellant's averments of unconstitutionality could not prevail and the mandatory sentence provisions of § 9713(a) were constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of sentence and held that evidence showed that appellant intended and did threaten the victim with a knife. The court ruled that in view of precedential authority to the contrary, appellant's boilerplate averments of unconstitutionality could not prevail and that the mandatory sentence provisions were constitutional.

 

419 of 892 DOCUMENTS


In re P.A.B.


No. 249 Harrisburg 1989


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


391 Pa. Super. 79; 570 A.2d 522; 1990 Pa. Super. LEXIS 85


September 28, 1989, Argued  
January 24, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargument Denied March 8, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order entered April 10, 1989, Court of Common Pleas, Adams County, Orphans' Court, Nos. RT-4-88; RT-5-88; & RT-6-88.



DISPOSITION: The order terminating the Parents' parental rights is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents, who were mentally retarded, sought review of the decision of the Court of Common Pleas, Adams County, Orphans' Court (Pennsylvania), which terminated their parental rights pursuant to Pa. Cons. Stat. 2511(a)(5).


OVERVIEW: Appellant parents' rights to their children were terminated by the state. The petition for termination did not designate a particular section of the Adoption Act, Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2511, et seq., under which termination was appropriate. The trial court entered conclusions of law and a decree nisi finding that the requisites of § 2511(a)(5) had been met. Appellants filed exceptions challenging the trial court's factual findings. The trial court dismissed the exceptions and rendered absolute the decree terminating appellants' parental rights. Appellants sought review arguing § 2511(a)(5) violated the equal protection and due process clauses, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, whether public policy mediated against the termination of parental rights in the absence of a finding of fault, and whether the evidence supported the termination of appellants' rights. The court reversed the order finding that to terminate appellants' rights would sever the relationship and injure the children and that upon applying § 2511(a)(5), maintaining the status quo best served the children's needs.


OUTCOME: The order terminating the parental rights of appellant parents' was reversed because no precedent existed that prevented the children from living outside appellants' home while maintaining a relationship with them, and no one advocated returning the children to appellants' custody. Since the children benefited from the relationship with appellants, and terminating their rights would injure the children, maintaining the status quo was best.

Commonwealth DOT v. Springbrook Transport, Inc.


No. 447 Philadelphia 1989


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


390 Pa. Super. 308; 568 A.2d 667; 1990 Pa. Super. LEXIS 59


October 25, 1989, Argued  
January 16, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County, Criminal Division at No. 646 Misc. 1988.



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, the Commonwealth's appeal is quashed and the case is remanded to the trial court for a determination of reasonable counsel fees. Jurisdiction is relinquished.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of an order by the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), which found appellant truck owner not guilty of violating the statute requiring motor vehicles to be registered in Pennsylvania.


OVERVIEW: Appellee truck owner was charged with, and found not guilty of, driving a motor vehicle without a Pennsylvania registration. The trial court found that appellee was exempt from the registration requirements. Appellant state sought review, alleging that the trial court erred as a matter of law by finding appellee exempt from registration. Appellee requested that the court quash the appeal, contending that a review of the verdict violated the double jeopardy clauses of U. S. Const. amend. V and Pa. Const. art. I, § 10, as the trial court's verdict amounted to an acquittal. The court quashed the appeal and held that it violated the double jeopardy clauses of both the state and federal constitutions. The court found that appellee was found not guilty of a criminal violation and that the jury's verdict was absolutely final, and immune from challenge. The court held that the appeal was patently frivolous, and that an award of attorney fees to appellee was justified.


OUTCOME: The court quashed appellant state's appeal because it violated the double jeopardy clauses of both the state and federal constitutions. The court found that because appellee truck owner was found not guilty of a criminal violation by a jury verdict that was absolutely final, the appeal was patently frivolous, and appellee was entitled to an award of attorney fees.

Custren v. Harleysville Ins. Co.


No. 01449 Philadelphia 1989


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


390 Pa. Super. 251; 568 A.2d 639; 1990 Pa. Super. LEXIS 4169


November 20, 1989, Submitted  
January 5, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order entered April 21, 1989, in the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Civil, No. 4278 April 1985.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurer sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Civil Division (Pennsylvania), that imposed sanctions on appellant for failure to settle a claim with appellee victim pursuant to Philadelphia, Pa. Local Rule 170, on the ground that the rule was unconstitutional, did not apply to first-party suits, and was not applicable to the case.


OVERVIEW: Appellant insurer refused to pay one of appellee victim's medical bills that resulted from a motor vehicle accident, claiming the treatment was not a necessary and reasonable expense. Appellee brought suit. The trial court held a settlement conference and concluded a reasonable settlement was the cost of the disputed bill. Appellant refused to pay and the trial court imposed Philadelphia, Pa. Local Rule 170 sanctions for failure to settle. The jury returned a verdict for the same amount and judgment was entered for that amount plus interest. Appellant argued that Rule 170 should not be applied because the jury's verdict was not 20 percent greater than the trial court's recommended settlement. Appellant argued that it was deprived of due process and the right to a jury trial, Rule 170 was unconstitutional because it duplicated provisions of rules and statutes, and that it did not apply to first-party lawsuits. The appellate court affirmed the order and held that Rule 170 sanctions were related to the amount of the final judgment, not to the amount of the jury verdict, was not excessively burdensome, and was not so similar to other rules to be duplicative.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order and held that Philadelphia, Pa. Local Rule 170 was applicable in an action between appellant insurer and appellee victim because the final judgment was more than 35 per cent greater than the recommended settlement. The court found the rule did not violate due process and right to trial by jury and was constitutional. The court declined to read limitations into the rule when limitations were not clearly specified.

Giacomucci v. Southeast Delco Sch. Dist.


No. 3060 C.D. 1998


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


742 A.2d 1165; 1999 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 895



December 23, 1999, Decided  
December 23, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed From No. 98-05805. Common Pleas Court of the County of Delaware. Judge BATTLE.
Giacomucci v. Southeast Delco Sch. Dist., 40 Pa. D. & C.4th 171, 40 Pa. D. & C.4th 171 (1998)



DISPOSITION: The order of the Delaware County Court of Common Pleas dated October 14, 1998 is hereby affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, school board of directors and district, challenged the order of Common Pleas Court of the County of Delaware (Pennsylvania) enjoining them, pursuant to Public School Code of 1949, 24 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 1-101 to 27-2702, from partially reimbursing tuition of private school or non-district public school children.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, school board and district, adopted a plan to partially reimburse tuition of children who attended private schools or non-district public schools. The trial court concluded that the Public School Code of 1949 (School Code), 24 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 1-101 to 27-2702 prohibited such a plan. Affirming and enjoining the implementation of the plan, the court held that pursuant to 24 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 610 the use or payment of any public school funds of any school district, in any manner or for any purpose not provided in the School Code was illegal. The appellants' plan to subsidize the education of school children choosing to attend private and non-district public schools was not authorized, expressly or impliedly by the School Code; thus, the appellants acted outside the scope of its statutory authority in adopting the plan.


OUTCOME: Affirmed and enjoined; appellants' plan to subsidize the education of school children choosing to attend private schools and non-district public schools was not authorized, expressly or impliedly, by the Public School Code; thus, was illegal.

PPG Indus. v. Commonwealth


No. 2355 C.D. 1987


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


1999 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1047


November 15, 1999, Argued  
November 30, 1999, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner manufacturer claimed the respondent Commonwealth's capital stock and franchise tax discriminated and petitioned the Pennsylvania Supreme Court for relief. The case was remanded to determine whether the tax imposed by 72 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 7602 was unconstitutional and the proper remedy.


OVERVIEW: The Supreme Court of Pennsylvania held that the § 7602 discriminated against interstate commerce and remanded the matter back to the commonwealth court to determine if the tax was compensatory. If it was not compensatory, it was unconstitutional and the commonwealth court had to determine the appropriate remedy. The parties agreed, and the commonwealth court held, that the tax was not a compensatory tax. After reviewing its options, the commonwealth court recommended the invalidation of § 7602(a) as it related to manufacturing within the State in the limited "headquarters context." The commonwealth court also recommended invalidation of the exemption in its entirety, but left the task of amending the tax to the legislature so that it could incorporate its intentions and constitutional considerations.


OUTCOME: The tax was not compensatory and was, therefore, unconstitutional. The commonwealth court recommended invalidation of a portion of the tax, and later invalidation of the entire exemption with amendment to be made by the legislature.

Commonwealth Ass'n of Sch. Adm'rs v. Board of Educ., School Dist.

COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Civil Division (Pennsylvania), denying its petition for review of an interest arbitration award issued by a panel of arbitrators pursuant to 71 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 371.


OVERVIEW: A panel of arbitrators was appointed pursuant to 71 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 371(d) when appellant school administrators and appellee school district could not agree on the terms of a new collective bargaining agreement. After an arbitration award was determined, appellant filed a petition for judicial review challenging the award, primarily on the grounds that the panel lacked jurisdiction to decide matters other than those submitted in writing by the parties. The trial court upheld the arbitration panel's award. On appeal, the court held that the arbitration panel did not exceed its authority because while 71 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 371(d) provided that appellee was required to give written notice to appellant containing specifications of disputed issues, appellant did not submit specific issues to the arbitration panel, but only broad proposals that essentially called into questions all the past practices of the parties.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed. The arbitration panel did not exceed its authority because while appellee was required to give written notice to appellant containing specifications of disputed issues, appellant did not submit specific issues to panel, but only broad proposals that called into questions all past practices of parties.

Watkins v. State Bd. of Dentistry


No. 819 C.D. 1999


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


740 A.2d 760; 1999 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 856


October 5, 1999, Submitted on Briefs, Argued  
November 8, 1999, Decided  
November 8, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed From No. 0360-46-97. State Agency: State Board of Dentistry.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of order of the respondent board (Pennsylvania) suspending his dental license and permit to administer analgesia upon finding that he engaged in unprofessional conduct and implementing regulations for, inter alia, failing to ensure that his office contained appropriate monitoring equipment for administration of general anesthesia.


OVERVIEW: A toddler died after receiving an injection of general anesthesia in petitioner's dental office. Thereafter, respondent board suspended petitioner's dental license after finding that he had not complied with its regulations by, inter alia, failing to have appropriate monitoring equipment in his office. On appeal, petitioner's primary contention was that respondent's regulation requiring appropriate monitoring equipment was unconstitutionally vague because it did not give him, or other practitioners, notice of what specific equipment was considered appropriate. The court agreed with petitioner, holding that the term "appropriate monitoring equipment" was unconstitutionally vague because it did not provide a reasonable standard by which petitioner was supposed to act. The court reasoned that the lack of clear guidance in respondent's regulation as to what constituted "appropriate" monitoring equipment would lead to a purely subjective criterion which may reflect merely the personal or professional views of individual members of respondent board.


OUTCOME: Order vacated, the term "appropriate monitoring equipment" was unconstitutionally vague because it did not provide a reasonable standard by which petitioner was supposed to act; case remanded for the imposition of reasonable sanctions based only on the remaining violations.

Simpson v. City of New Castle

COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA

September 10, 1999, Submitted on Briefs  
November 3, 1999, Decided  
November 3, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Common Pleas Court of the County of Lawrence. Judge PRATT. Appealed From No. 40134 of 1998, EQ.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appeal from an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lawrence County (Pennsylvania) denying appellant's request to permanently enjoin respondent city from enforcing certain provisions of city ordinance requiring landlords to register residential rental property that they own within the city.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged the denial of his request to permanently enjoin respondent city from enforcing certain city ordinance provisions, New Castle (Pennsylvania) Council Bill 1998-11 §§ PM-901 through PM-907, that required landlords to register residential rental property that they owned within the city. The appellate court affirmed the denial, concluding that there was no ground to challenge for unreasonable search and seizure under the federal or state constitutions because none of the challenged provisions automatically resulted in an inspection of the property without the owner's consent; there was no due process violation because appellant was provided with adequate opportunity to challenge any adverse decision with regard to his property; and there was no double taxation because the required permit fee was not a tax.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed because no constitutional violations existed for unreasonable search as none of challenged provisions automatically resulted in inspection of property without consent; no due process violation because appellant was provided opportunity to challenge adverse decision with regard to property; no double taxation because permit fee was not tax.

In re Substitute Nomination Certificate of Moran


No. 2702 C.D. 1999


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


739 A.2d 1168; 1999 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 845


October 27, 1999, Argued  
October 29, 1999, Decided  
October 29, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Case Name Amended by the Court November 4, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed From No. 99 - Civil - 3934. Common Pleas Court of the County of Lancaster. Judge Walsh.



DISPOSITION: The Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lackawanna County dated October 20, 1999 is REVERSED and the Substitute Nomination Certificate of Michael A. Moran as Lackawanna County Reform Committee Candidate for District Justice, Magisterial District 45-3-04 is set aside. The Lackawanna County Board of Elections is DIRECTED to refrain from tabulating any votes cast for Michael A. Moran on absentee ballots for the November 2, 1999 Municipal Election. The Lackawanna County Board of Elections is further DIRECTED to lock the lever for Michael A. Moran as Lackawanna County Reform Committee Candidate for District Justice, Magisterial District 45-3-04, on all voting machines on which his name appears.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the Common Pleas Court of the County of Lancaster (Pennsylvania) dismissing his objections to the substitution of appellee as the Reform Committee candidate for district justice, where appellee had run unsuccessfully for the Democratic and Republican Party nominations for the same position.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, the nominated candidate of the Democratic Party for the office of county district justice, appealed from the trial court's dismissal of his objections to the substitute nomination certificate of appellee as the candidate of an independent political body for the same office. Appellee ran unsuccessfully for both the Democratic and Republican nominations for district justice. On appeal, the court reversed. Because the substitute nomination was made by a political body rather than a political party, it was governed by 25 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2940, which prohibited substitution of an individual who had been a candidate for nomination by any political party for any office, whether or not nominated for such office. The court further found that 25 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2940 was not unconstitutional because it was a legitimate effort to provide clear choices to the electorate and to preclude so-called "sore-loser" candidacies.


OUTCOME: Order dismissing objections to appellee's substitute nomination for district judge reversed, because appellee could not be substituted as the nominee of a political body after unsuccessfully running for the nomination of the Democratic and Republican Parties.

Shaulis v. Pennsylvania State Ethics Comm'n


NO. 991 C.D. 1999


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


739 A.2d 1091; 1999 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 824


June 16, 1999, Submitted on Briefs, Argued  
October 20, 1999, Decided  
October 20, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected October 21, 1999. Petition for Allowance of Appeal Granted April 11, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Pa. LEXIS 908.
Corrected by, 10/21/1999
Appeal granted by Shaulis v. Pennsylvania State Ethics Comm'n, 561 Pa. 212, 749 A.2d 910, 2000 Pa. LEXIS 908 (2000)
Affirmed by Shaulis v. Pa. State Ethics Comm'n, 2003 Pa. LEXIS 1792 (Pa., Oct. 1, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed From: No. 99-003 State Agency: State Ethics Commission.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of an opinion of respondent, State Ethics Commission, pursuant to the Public Official and Employee Ethics Act, 65 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1103(g); respondent motioned to quash petitioner's appeal and motion to strike portions of respondent's brief on the merits in opposition to petition for review.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner retired from the Pennsylvania Department of Revenue, requesting advice from respondent, Pennsylvania State Ethics Commission, as to what extent the Public Official and Employee Ethics Act (Act), 65 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1103(g), imposed restrictions upon an attorney following retirement in publishing articles and/or books. Respondent held that petitioner was subject to the Act, that restrictions applied to restrict former public officials/public employees even as to practicing law before their former governmental body. Respondent's March 24, 1999 opinion was an adjudication pursuant to the Administrative Agency Law, 2 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 101. The opinion affected petitioner's right to practice her profession, and was thus available for judicial review. The Act did not control the conduct of an attorney in rendering professional legal services to clients before his or her former governmental body. The only entity that could prohibit an attorney from practicing law was the Supreme Court.


OUTCOME: Motion to quash appeal by respondent denied; motion to strike portions of respondent's brief granted; adjudication of respondent reversed; statutory provisions did not control the conduct of an attorney in rendering professional legal services to clients before his or her former governmental body.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner petitioned for review of an order of the State Board of Funeral Directors Board directing petitioner to pay a civil penalty for violating 49 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 13.193 in a freedom of commercial speech action.


OVERVIEW: An investigator for State Board of Funeral Directors Board (Board) cited petitioner for violating Board regulations because he failed to include his name as permanent supervisor of funeral home in published newspaper advertisements. Giordano v. Ridge


No. 103 M.D. 1999


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


737 A.2d 350; 1999 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 697


May 19, 1999, Argued  
August 31, 1999, Decided  
August 31, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Order of the Commonwealth Court Affirmed June 20, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Pa. LEXIS 1513.



DISPOSITION:  [**1] Respondents' preliminary objections in the nature of a demurrer are sustained. Taxpayer's petition for review fails to state a cause of action upon which the requested relief may be granted. Taxpayer's petition for review in the nature of a complaint for declaratory judgment and injunctive relief is dismissed with prejudice.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed for review in the nature of an action seeking declaratory and injunctive relief against respondents claiming that the Capital Facilities Debt Enabling Act, 72 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 3919.100-3919.5102 (1999), violated Pa. Const. art. VIII.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner claimed that the Capital Facilities Debt Enabling Act, 72 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 3919.101-3919.5102 (1999) (Act 1), violated Pa. Const. art. VIII by unconstitutionally incurring debt on behalf of the state and/or by pledging the credit of the state to an individual, corporation, or association. Respondents filed preliminary objections in the nature of a demurrer alleging petitioner failed to state a claim sufficient to permit an award of the relief requested. The language of Pa. Const. art. VIII did not prohibit loans from the state to a municipal authority, even when the ultimate beneficiary was a private entity. Under Act 1, the money flowed from the state to a municipality or municipal authority and not directly to the private entity. Petitioner failed to state a claim of unconstitutional incursion of debt or pledging of the credit of the state.


OUTCOME: Respondents' preliminary objections in the nature of a demurrer were sustained. Petition for review failed to state a cause of action upon which requested relief, declaratory judgment and injunctive relief, could be granted, and so was dismissed with prejudice.

Hutchinson v. Pennsylvania State Emples. Retirement Bd.


3016 C.D. 1998


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA

April 15, 1999, Submitted On Briefs  
August 6, 1999, Decided  
August 6, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied March 21, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Pa. LEXIS 673.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed From No. 1997-12. State Agency Pennsylvania State Employees' Retirement Board.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appeal by petitioner of an order of the State Employes' Retirement Board (Pennsylvania) granting only in part petitioner's request for interest on death benefit payable from petitioner's husband's retirement account, but denying her request for attorney's fees.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner sought a death benefit from her husband's retirement account that was payable to her due to her status as her husband's principal beneficiary. Petitioner contended that the State Employes' Retirement Board (SERB) erred in affirming an award of interest for a period of 39 days rather than for a period of 235 days. The court affirmed, observing that petitioner's husband was not an active member of the State Employes' Retirement System at the time of his death. It could not be said that SERB wrongfully withheld benefits due petitioner when its duty to pay benefits either did not yet arise or was to be performed within a reasonable period of time. The award of 39 days' interest was based on a reasonable and proper construction of the contract underlying petitioner's entitlement to death benefits and state law.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed. The State Employes' Retirement Board (SERB) committed no error in denying petitioner's request for additional interest on death benefits. Because it was not ripe for review, the court declined to address petitioner's argument that she was entitled to attorney's fees.

Penn's Grant Assocs. v. Northampton County Bd. of Assessment Appeals


No. 3427 C.D. 1998


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


733 A.2d 23; 1999 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 508


May 18, 1999, Argued  
June 22, 1999, Decided  
June 22, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed From No. 1996-C-05214, 1996-C-05215, 1996-C-05216 and 1997-C-06093. Common Pleas Court of the County of Northampton. Judge BARATTA.



DISPOSITION: The order of the Court of Common Pleas of Northampton County dated November 24, 1998, is affirmed in part and reversed in part. The case is remanded to the trial court to take into consideration the indirect costs in valuing Phases II - IV, but is affirmed as to Phase I because Taxpayer failed to present evidence to rebut the prima facie validity of the assessment. Jurisdiction is relinquished.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Northampton County (Pennsylvania), which found that it had failed to provide any competent, relevant evidence to reverse the tax assessment placed on lots contained in phase one of appellant's planned residential development.


OVERVIEW: Appellant taxpayer began improving lots in a proposed four-phase residential development project. Unsatisfied with the tax assessments of the lots, the taxpayer appealed to appellee board, and then to the trial court. Appellant contended that the trial court erred in finding that an assessment had to be made on every individual lot in phase one of its development once a lot was sold. The court found that once lots were sold from phase one, that phase had to be assessed on an individual lot basis. Consequently, the court affirmed phase one assessments because appellant, who needed to challenge the value and give a value to each individual lot rather than the entire phase, failed to present sufficient evidence to rebut the prima facie validity of appellee's assessment. The case was remanded to the trial court to take into consideration the indirect costs in valuing phases two through four.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed in part. Phase one assessments were proper because appellant failed to present sufficient evidence to rebut the prima facie validity of appellee's assessment. The order was reversed in part and remanded to the trial court to take into consideration the indirect costs in valuing development phases two through four.

 

434 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Dial v. Vaughn


No. 995 M.D. 1997


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


733 A.2d 1; 1999 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 432


September 16, 1998, Submitted On Briefs  
May 20, 1999, Decided  
May 20, 1999, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [**1] The preliminary objections to the amended petition for review are hereby sustained and the petition is hereby dismissed for failure to state a claim upon which relief may be granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged the constitutionality of a requirement, under DNA Detection of Sexual and Violent Offenders Act (Act), 35 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 7651.306(b), that appellant submit a blood sample for DNA testing. Appellant argued the Act violated the doctrine of separation of power, was unreasonable search and seizure under U.S. Const. amend. IV, violated ex post facto prohibitions of Pa. Const. art. I, § 17 and U.S. Const. art I, § 10.


OVERVIEW: Appellant inmate raised various constitutional challenges to the requirement under DNA Detection of Sexual and Violent Offenders Act (Act), 35 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 7651.306(b), that appellant submit a blood sample for DNA testing. The court held Act did not violate separation of powers doctrine because the legislature had not affected appellant's eligibility for parole or altered the length of his sentence. The court held that Act was not an unconstitutional ex post facto enhancement of appellant's sentence. There was no ex post factor violation if the Act was not penal in nature but merely procedural. Act, § 306, permitting denial of parol for refusal to comply with Act's sample collection requirement, was not ex post facto sentence enhancement. Infliction of an additional punishment, within the parameters of appellant's original sentence, was not ex post facto. The court held Act's requirement for blood sample was not a violation of U.S. Const. amend. IV when balanced against the government's interest in furthering a legitimate need. Blood testing was a relatively minimal intrusion, which was outweighed by the special public interest in maintaining an identification data bank.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed appellant inmate's petition because DNA Act's blood sample requirement did not violate separation of powers doctrine when appellant's sentence was not affected. No ex post facto violation when provisions of DNA Act were not penal in nature but merely procedural. DNA Act's requirement for blood sample did not violate the Fourth Amendment because testing was a minimal intrusion when balanced against a legitimate public need.

 

435 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Maierhoffer v. GLS Capital, Inc.


No. 3465 C.D. 1998


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


730 A.2d 547; 1999 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 426


February 10, 1999, Argued  
May 14, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied and Petitioner's Motion for Leave to Submit Relevant Case Law Denied January 20, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Pa. LEXIS 159.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed From No. 98-18554. Common Pleas Court of the County of Allegheny.



DISPOSITION: The order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County in the above captioned matter is hereby affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the Common Pleas Court of the County of Allegheny (Pennsylvania) that dismissed her complaint against appellee county with prejudice. The complaint alleged a county could not assign its tax liens.


OVERVIEW: After appellant failed to pay property taxes on her real property for several years, appellee county secured a lien against the property, which it assigned to appellee corporation. Appellee corporation was granted judgment against appellant for the back taxes, penalties, and interest and subsequently scheduled a sheriff's sale of the property. Appellant filed a class action complaint against appellees, which the trial court dismissed. On appeal, appellant asserted the trial court erred in concluding that municipal tax liens are assignable under the Municipal Claims and Tax Liens Act (Act), 53 P.S. §§ 7101-7505 (Pennsylvania). The court disagreed and held that under the general rules of statutory construction, the Act's use of the word "any" included both tax claims and municipal claims as claims which a municipality could assign to a party that was a stranger to the original transaction. The court therefore affirmed the order of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court dismissing appellant's class action because appellee county had the statutory right to assign both tax liens and municipal claims to any party that was a stranger to the original transaction.

Richards v. Unemployment Compensation Bd. of Review


No. 2085 C.D. 1998


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


731 A.2d 214; 1999 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 369


February 11, 1999, Argued  
May 6, 1999, Decided  
May 6, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed From No. B-365117. State Agency, Unemployment Compensation Board of Review.



DISPOSITION: The order of the Unemployment Compensation Board of Review, dated June 3, 1998, at No. B-365117, is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner claimant sought review of an order of respondent Pennsylvania Unemployment Compensation Board of Review (UCBR), which reversed the decision of a referee granting claimant benefits. Claimant contended that the UCBR erred in determining that claimant was not entitled to move his base year for eligibility purposes pursuant to § 204(b) of the Workers' Compensation Act, 77 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 71(b).


OVERVIEW: Petitioner claimant received workers' compensation benefits, and later applied for unemployment compensation benefits, which were denied. Respondent Unemployment Compensation Board of Review (UCBR) determined that claimant failed to meet the eligibility requirements under § 401(a) of the Unemployment Compensation Law (Law), 43 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 801(a). The UCBR determined that claimant's failure to meet unemployment compensation financial criteria was not due to a compensable injury as required by § 204(b) of the Workers' Compensation Act, (Act), 77 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 71(b), and that claimant was ineligible for unemployment benefits. On appeal, the court held that an applicant for unemployment compensation, who received compensation for a workers' compensation injury during his base year, was entitled to move his base year for eligibility purposes pursuant to § 204(b) and § 401(a). The court reversed, finding that claimant had received workers' compensation benefits for his work-related injury during his base year and had a work-related injury compensable under § 204(b). The employer's contention that § 204(b) violated Pa. Const. art. III, § 3 was without merit.


OUTCOME: The order of the Unemployment Compensation Board of Review (UCBR) was reversed. The court concluded that the UCBR erred in determining that claimant was not entitled to move his base year for eligibility purposes where claimant received workers' compensation benefits for the period in question; therefore, claimant was entitled to move his base year.
