Conley Motor Inns, Inc. v. Township of Penn


No. 2088 C.D. 1998


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


728 A.2d 1012; 1999 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 271


February 11, 1999, Argued  
April 15, 1999, Decided  
April 15, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied October 22, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Pa. LEXIS 3167.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed From No. EQ 97-50022. Common Pleas Court of the County of Butler. Judge DOERR.



DISPOSITION: The order of the Court of Common Pleas of Butler County, dated June 30, 1998, at E.Q. No. 97-50022, is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of the order of the Common Pleas Court of the County of Butler (Pennsylvania) denying appellants' petition for review filed pursuant to the Declaratory Judgments Act of Pennsylvania, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 7531 - 7541, which challenged the validity of a local amusement tax ordinance.


OVERVIEW: Appellant taxpayers operated public, for-profit golf courses and appealed the order denying an appeal of a local amusement tax ordinance enacted by appellee township. The ordinance assessed a tax on appellants' facilities because the facilities charged admission, but exempted any activities that the ordinance declared exempt. Appellants alleged that the ordinance was unconstitutional and violated appellants' rights under the U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1 and Pa. Const. art. VIII, § 1. The appellate court affirmed and held that appellee acted within its discretion in implementing the amusement tax. The ordinance was presumed constitutional and appellants failed to establish that the ordinance plainly violated the constitution. The ordinance did not treat similarly situated entities differently but distinguished between admission fees charged at private, nonprofit entities and public, for-profit entities. The appellate court found that the status and purposes of the entities were different and that appellee had a rational basis for excluding private, non-profit entities from the tax.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying appellants' petition for review which challenged the validity of a local amusement tax ordinance and held that appellee had a rational basis for differentiating between appellants and private, nonprofit entities.

 

438 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Cruz v. Workers' Compensation Appeal Bd. (Philadelphia Club)


No. 1296 C.D. 1998


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


728 A.2d 413; 1999 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 253


March 11, 1999, Argued  
April 13, 1999, Decided  
April 13, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed From No. A97-1197. State Agency Workers' Compensation Appeal Board.



DISPOSITION: The order of the Workers' Compensation Appeal Board is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners appealed from an order of the State Agency Workers' Compensation Appeals Board, dismissing provider's petition for review of an adverse utilization review determination related to claimant's workers' compensation action.


OVERVIEW: Claimant was injured in the course of his employment. Claimant was treated by provider, his physician, for the injury. Claimant brought a workers' compensation action, and the workers' compensation judge (WCJ) found, after admitting deposition testimony from another physician, that provider's treatment of claimant was unreasonable. Petitioners, claimant and provider, appealed from an order dismissing provider's petition for review of the adverse utilization review (UR) determination. The court ruled that if a party failed to abide by the time limits set forth in 34 Pa. Code § 131.66, then the evidence could not be admitted, relied upon, or utilized in the proceedings or referee rulings pursuant to 34 Pa. Code § 131.63. Further, the court held that as the testifying physician's deposition was taken over four months before provider filed his petition for review of the UR determination, the deposition was not taken in compliance with the time requirements and should not have been admitted or relied upon by the WCJ. The court reversed the order, concluding that the WCJ erred in relying on the deposition in the UR proceedings as it represented inadmissible hearsay.


OUTCOME: In a workers' compensation action, the order dismissing provider's petition for review of an adverse utilization review determination was reversed where there was no competent evidence in the record excluding the inadmissible hearsay suggesting an alternative treatment to maintain claimant's functional level and to manage his pain. There was no competent evidence to establish that provider's treatment was unreasonable or unnecessary.

Society Created to Reduce Urban Blight (SCRUB) v. Zoning Bd. of Adjustment


No. 3315 C.D. 1997


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


729 A.2d 117; 1999 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 234


March 9, 1999, Argued  
April 5, 1999, Decided  
April 5, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reargument denied by, 06/03/1999
Related proceeding at Soc'y Created to Reduce Urban Blight v. Zoning Bd. of Adjustment, 772 A.2d 1040, 2001 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 265 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2001)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed From No. 9703-0145, 9703-0148 and 9703-0150. Common Pleas Court of the County of Philadelphia Judge LEVIN.
Society Created to Reduce Urban Blight v. Zoning Bd. of Adjustment, 1998 Phila. Cty. Rptr. LEXIS 9 (Pa. C.P., 1998)



DISPOSITION: The order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County dated November 6, 1997, at Nos. 9703-0145, 9703-0148 and 9703-0150, is reversed and the case remanded to the trial court for a determination of the merits of Protestors' appeal. Jurisdiction relinquished.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, including an organization against urban blight, sought review of an order from the Common Pleas Court of the County of Philadelphia (Pennsylvania) that quashed their appeal from a city zoning board of adjustment decision granting a variance to appellees for the erection of outdoor signs. The trial court held that appellants lacked standing to challenge the decision.


OVERVIEW: An order that quashed appellants' request for review of a city zoning board of adjustment decision was reversed, and the case was remanded for consideration of the merits. Appellants, including individuals and groups interested in preventing urban blight, opposed appellees' request for a variance to allow the erection of outdoor signs. Holding that appellants lacked standing, the board granted appellees' request, finding that the requisite showing of undue hardship had been demonstrated and that all of the criteria under Pa. Municipalities Planning Code (Code) § 14-1802(1) had been met. In quashing the appeal, the trial court found that appellants had failed to demonstrate that they were specifically harmed by the granting of the variance because they did not live or represent anyone living in the vicinity of the proposed signs. The appellate court held that it was within the city's power to provide in Code § 14-1806(1) for taxpayer standing to challenge city zoning actions. Because appellants were either taxpayers or organizations that represented taxpayers, the appellate court found that the trial court erred in affirming the board's decision that appellants lacked standing.


OUTCOME: An order quashing appellants' request for review of a city zoning board of adjustment ruling was reversed, and the case was remanded for a determination of the merits. Because it was within the city's power to provide for taxpayer standing to challenge zoning actions, and appellants were either taxpayers or organizations that represented taxpayers, the trial court erred in upholding the board's decision that appellants did not have standing.

 

440 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Pennsylvania Prison Soc'y v. Commonwealth


No. 893 M.D. 1997


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


727 A.2d 632; 1999 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 215


November 18, 1998, Argued  
March 22, 1999, Decided  
March 22, 1999, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [**1] The motion for judgment on the pleadings filed by the Pennsylvania Prison Society et al. is GRANTED. The motion for judgment on the pleadings filed by the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania et al. is DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Cross-motions for judgment on the pleadings were filed in a case challenging the validity of a change in the state constitution that would require a unanimous recommendation of the Board of Pardons before the Governor could pardon or commute the sentence of someone sentenced to death or life imprisonment, along with other changes.


OVERVIEW: The court granted petitioner organization's motion for judgment on the pleadings and denied defendant state's motion for judgment on the pleadings in petitioner's claim that a ballot amendment to the state constitution was unconstitutional. The vote could not validate anything that violated a provision of the constitution. Pa. Const. art. XI, § 1 required that two or more proposed amendments to the constitution had to be voted on separately. A natural reading of the constitution made the ballot proposition unconstitutional because it described four amendments and did not describe a fifth. An imprecise ballot description of the amendment violated 25 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2621.1 in that it failed to explain the full ramifications of the changes or why such changes might be needed.


OUTCOME: The court granted petitioner's motion for judgment on the pleadings and denied respondent's motion for judgment on the pleadings because multiple changes had been improperly combined into one amendment and because the citizens were entitled to clear notice of what the amendment entailed.

 

441 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Silo v. Ridge


No. 468 M.D. 1998


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


728 A.2d 394; 1999 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 237



March 12, 1999, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [**1] Respondents' Preliminary Objections are sustained and Petitioner's Complaint seeking Declaratory Judgment is hereby dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate brought an action against respondent government officials seeking a declaratory judgment holding the Prison Medical Services Act, 61 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 1001-1017, and the Pennsylvania Department of Corrections' Policy Bulletin DC-ADM 820 to be unconstitutional and invalid.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner inmate brought an action against respondent government officials alleging that the Prison Medical Services Act (Act), 61 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 1001-1017, and the Pennsylvania Department of Corrections' Policy Bulletin DC-ADM 820 was unconstitutional and invalid. The court dismissed petitioner's complaint and held petitioner lacked standing. Because petitioner did not allege that he was or probably would be affected by the Act or the policy bulletin, petitioner's complaint failed to state a cause of action. Petitioner did not establish that prison officials were deliberately indifferent to his serious medical needs, and thus could not show any violation of U.S. Const. amend. VIII. Requiring inmates to pay a minimal fee for their medical care did not amount to deliberate indifference. Petitioner failed to show a U.S. Const. amend. XIV violation, as he did not allege that he was deprived of life, liberty, or property. Petitioner did not show a violation of the Administrative Agency law, as he failed to show respondents rendered an adjudication. The Act and the policy bulletin did not violate the prohibition against ex post facto laws and bills of attainder.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed petitioner inmate's complaint and held that petitioner was not entitled to declaratory relief because the complaint did not allege an actual case or controversy between petitioner and respondent government officials, and petitioner's complaint failed to state a cause of action.

 

442 of 892 DOCUMENTS


In re Barkman


No. 1713 C.D. 1998


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


726 A.2d 440; 1999 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 247



March 12, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied July 13, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Pa. LEXIS 1978. Certiorari Denied November 15, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 7547.



DISPOSITION: The order of the Court of Common Pleas of Bedford County is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Bedford County (Pennsylvania), denying her oral petition to compel the trial court to permit her to vote any available ballot in a state primary election despite appellant's lack of registration with either the Republican or Democratic political party.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, an independent voter not associated with either the Democratic or the Republican party, challenged the trial court's denial of her oral petition to compel the local election board to permit her to cast her vote in a state primary election being held that day. The trial court concluded that § 702 of the Pennsylvania Election Code, 25 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2812 (1937), which restricted the right to vote in any party's primary elections to those persons registered as members of such party, did not violate appellant's constitutional rights of free association, to vote, or to equal protection of the laws. On appeal, the court agreed. As a registered non-partisan voter, appellant claimed not that the state's voter registration requirements were onerous but that they resulted in disenfranchisement of principled voters who desired no ongoing affiliation with a particular political party. The court followed controlling United States Supreme Court precedent and held that the type of interest asserted by appellant did not outweigh the interests of political parties and the state as embodied in a duly-enacted closed method of conducting primary elections. The court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of appellant's oral petition seeking the right to vote in a state primary election even though appellant was not registered with either the Republican or Democratic party. The state statute permitting only party-affiliated voters to cast ballots in the primary election did not effectively disenfranchise appellant or rob her of her constitutional right to freely associate.

Unisys Corp. v. Commonwealth


No. 151 F.R. 1991, No. 201 F.R. 1993, No. 202 F.R. 1993


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


726 A.2d 1096; 1999 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 154


May 6, 1998, Argued  
March 8, 1999, Decided  
March 8, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended March 12, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed From No. R-13,575, C-18,153 and C-17,792. State Agency Board of Finance and Revenue.



DISPOSITION: The orders of the Board of Finance and Revenue in the above captioned matters are hereby reversed. The Chief Clerk is directed to remand this case to the Department of Revenue for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner corporation sought review of three orders of the Board of Finance and Revenue (Pennsylvania) which affirmed the Department of Revenue's settlement of petitioner corporation's franchise tax and petitioner's obligation as successor corporation to another corporation's franchise tax.


OVERVIEW: The court considered whether the interstate commerce and due process clauses required the state to include property, payroll and sales of subsidiaries in the three-factor apportionment formula and, if not, whether the state statutory scheme mandated administrative relief. It concluded that petitioner corporation had not met its burden as to its constitutional claims. Petitioner corporation had not demonstrated a due process violation where it asserted that if the total property, payroll and sales of the unitary business enterprise were included in the fractions of the three-factor formula, its tax due would be approximately 44.5 percent less than the figure arrived at by the Board of Finance and Review (Board). The court held that a variance of this magnitude between the allocated and actual shares of petitioner's activity in the state, although not of constitutional proportions, required statutory relief under 72 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 7401(3)2.(a)(18). Thus, the court reversed the orders of the Board and remanded for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded, finding that a variance of 44.5 percent between the allocated and actual shares of a corporation's activity in the state was of a magnitude that required statutory relief from the assessed franchise tax.

Slater v. Pennsylvania Dep't of Educ.


No. 2447 C.D. 1997


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA

DISPOSITION: The order of the Professional Standards and Practices Commission, dated August 11, 1997, at No. DI-97-14, is hereby reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of respondent education commission's decision that suspended petitioner's professional teaching certification, without a meaningful pre-deprivation or post-deprivation hearing, based solely on the existence of an indictment against petitioner that involved crimes of moral turpitude.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner challenged a decision of respondent education commission (commission) that suspended her professional teaching certification without a meaningful pre-deprivation or post-deprivation hearing after she was indicted on moral turpitude charges. The appellate court reversed the decision of respondent commission. Suspension of petitioner's teaching certification solely because an indictment alleging moral turpitude existed against petitioner violated her constitutional due process rights as she was deprived of a property interest without a proper hearing.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed a decision of respondent education commission that suspended, without a meaningful pre-deprivation or post-deprivation hearing, petitioner's professional teaching certification after an indictment charging moral turpitude was filed against her. Petitioner's minimum due process rights were deprived when, without a proper hearing, her property interest in her teaching certification was removed.

Correll v. DOT, Bureau of Driver Licensing


No. 496 C.D. 1998


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


726 A.2d 427; 1999 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 76


October 7, 1998, Argued  
February 18, 1999, Decided  
February 18, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Granted March 23, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Pa. LEXIS 591.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed From No. 97-09631. Common Pleas Court of the County of Chester. Judge RILEY, Jr.



DISPOSITION: The order of the Court of Common Pleas of Chester County is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the Common Pleas Court of the County of Chester (Pennsylvania), which denied her appeal and reinstated a one-year suspension of her operating privileges imposed pursuant to the Interstate Compact, section 1581 of the Vehicle Code, 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1581.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed a judgment which reinstated a one-year suspension of appellant's operating privileges imposed pursuant to the Interstate Compact, 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1581, and which denied her appeal. Appellant licensed Pennsylvania driver was convicted in New Jersey for driving while under the influence of alcohol (DUI). New Jersey notified the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania in compliance with the Interstate Compact, and appellant's Pennsylvania license was suspended for one year as a result of the New Jersey conviction. The court rejected appellant's argument that the Interstate Compact violated the double jeopardy, due process, and equal protection clauses of the United States and Pennsylvania constitutions. First, driving was a privilege and not a right. Second, the suspension of appellant's driver's license was a collateral civil consequence of her DUI conviction and, thus, did not constitute punishment within the meaning of the double jeopardy clauses. Finally, appellant could not maintain a claim for discriminatory enforcement of a facially neutral statute like the Interstate Compact without evidence of a discriminatory effect and discriminatory purpose.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment, which reinstated a one-year suspension of appellant's operating privileges imposed pursuant to the Interstate Compact and which denied her appeal. Appellant's challenges to the constitutionality of the Interstate Compact on the grounds that it violated the double jeopardy, due process, and equal protection clauses of the state and federal constitutions were without merit.

Lucas v. Workers' Compensation Appeal Bd.(Kleen All of Am., Inc.)


No. 2691 C.D. 1998


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


727 A.2d 599; 1999 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 74


December 31, 1998, Submitted On Briefs

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Granted November 8, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Pa. LEXIS 3334. Order of the commonwealth Court Reversed June 19, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Pa. LEXIS 1504.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed From No. A96-2095. State Agency, Workers' Compensation Appeal Board.



DISPOSITION: The order of the Workers' Compensation Appeal Board dated September 16, 1998, at No. A96-2095, is reversed insofar as it allowed suspension of payments to Provider from Employer's filing of the Utilization Review Petition on December 27, 1994, through the WCJ's decision on May 29, 1996, and remanded for a calculation of medical payments to be paid to Provider. Jurisdiction relinquished.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Claimant appealed from an order of the Pennsylvania Workers' Compensation Appeal Board affirming the decision of the Workers' Compensation Judge finding that medical benefit payments by claimant's employer to claimant's health care provider could be discontinued because his medical treatment of claimant was no longer reasonable nor necessary.


OVERVIEW: The court reversed in part an order of the Pennsylvania Workers' Compensation Appeal Board (Board) affirming the decision of the Workers' Compensation Judge (WCJ) finding that medical benefit payments by claimant's employer to claimant's health care provider could be discontinued because his medical treatment of claimant was no longer reasonable nor necessary. The order was reversed insofar as it allowed suspension of payments to provider from the date of employer's filing of a Utilization Review Petition through the WCJ's decision pursuant to the supersedeas provisions of the Workers' Compensation Act, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 77, § 531(5) and § 531(6). On appeal, claimant successfully contended that based on the Sullivan decision, the Board erred by allowing suspension of medical payments to provider prior to the WCJ's determination. The Sullivan court held that the supersedeas provisions violated constitutional due process protections under U.S. Const. amend. XIV because they allowed employers to stop payments for medical treatments pending review before giving employees an opportunity to dispute the allegations.


OUTCOME: The court reversed in part an order of the Pennsylvania Workers' Compensation Appeal Board insofar as it allowed suspension of medical benefit payments to provider from the date of employer's filing of a Utilization Review Petition through the date of the Workers' Compensation Judge's decision. The supersedeas provisions of the Workers' Compensation Act, which allowed the suspension, violated claimant's procedural due process rights.

 

447 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Wilson Partners, L.P. v. Commonwealth


No. 355 F.R. 1996, No. 356 F.R. 1996


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


723 A.2d 1079; 1999 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 36


December 9, 1998, Argued  
January 26, 1999, Decided  
January 26, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed From No. 27327 and 27329. State Agency Board of Finance and Revenue.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner taxpayers sought review of the orders of the State Agency Board of Finance and Revenue denying their petitions for refunds of realty transfer tax payments. Petitioners argued that the Pennsylvania Realty Transfer Tax Act, 72 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 8101-C - 8113-C, unconstitutionally imposed an unequal tax burden on a nonexempt party who entered into a taxable real estate transaction with an exempt party.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner taxpayers entered into sale and purchase agreements with a federal government agency. At the time the deeds were recorded, petitioners paid the realty transfer tax. Petitioners later requested refunds of the tax paid. When respondent agency denied their petitions for refund, petitioners sought review in the courts. Petitioners argued that the Pennsylvania Realty Transfer Tax Act, 72 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 8101-C - 8113-C, unconstitutionally imposed an unequal tax burden on a nonexempt party who entered into a taxable real estate transaction with an exempt party and discriminated against the federal government in violation of the Supremacy Clause of the U.S. Const. The court affirmed the decision. The court ruled that the statute did not impose twice the normal tax liability on a nonexempt party because liability for payment of the realty transfer tax was joint and several, dischargeable by the parties. The court further ruled that the statute did not impermissibly discriminate against the government because parties who transacted with the United States were no worse off than nonexempt parties who transacted with other nonexempt parties.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders of the State Agency Board of Finance and Revenue denying petitioners' requests for refunds of realty transfer tax payments. The court held that the Pennsylvania Realty Transfer Tax Act did not impose twice the normal tax liability on a nonexempt party because liability for a realty transfer tax payment was joint and several, dischargeable by the parties.

 

448 of 892 DOCUMENTS


City of Philadelphia v. FOP, Lodge No. 5


No. 2756 C.D. 1996, No. 2642 C.D. 1996


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


723 A.2d 747; 1999 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 37


October 8, 1997, Argued  
January 26, 1999, Decided  
January 26, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed From No. 3545 June Term, 1995. Common Pleas Court of the County of Philadelphia. Judge DiBONA, JR.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed, and the City will compensate eligible uniformed employees at the rate of 75% of their gross pay for the closed period of July 1, 1992 through May 31, 1994; and compensate said employees at the rate of 80% of their gross pay for the period from June 1, 1994 through June 30, 1996.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant unions sought review of the order of the Common Pleas Court of the County of Philadelphia (Pennsylvania) granting a motion for disposition on the merits in favor of appellee city and city officials. Before the court was whether the Heart and Lung Act, 53 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 637-638, required appellee city to compensate eligible employees at 100 percent of their gross pay or 100 percent of the injured employee's net pay.


OVERVIEW: Appellant fire fighters and police officers' unions sought review of the lower court's ruling that an employee's net wages after taxes constituted the "full rate of salary" for purposes of the Heart and Lung Act, 53 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 637-638. Before the appellate court was whether appellee city was required to compensate eligible employees at 100 percent of their gross pay or whether the rate of compensation should be 100 percent of the injured employee's net pay. The appellate court reversed the lower court's judgment. The appellate court held that the Heart and Lung Act clearly provided that eligible employees were to be compensated at their "full rate of salary," which the appellate court interpreted as gross pay. However, because of collective bargaining agreements, appellee city was not required to retroactively compensate temporarily injured uniformed employees at a rate of 100 percent of their gross pay. The appellate court ruled that the parties were bound by the arbitration decisions pursuant to their collective bargaining agreements and ordered appellee city to compensate eligible uniformed employees up to 80 percent of their gross pay for the time period in question.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the lower court's order and ordered appellee city to compensate eligible uniformed employees up to 80 percent of their gross pay. The appellate court concluded that the Heart and Lung Act provided that eligible employees were to be compensated at their full rate of salary but held that the arbitration decisions issued pursuant to the parties' collective bargaining agreements were controlling.

Tri-State Transfer Co. v. Department of Envtl. Protection Tinicum Twp.


No. 55 C.D. 1998, No. 291 C.D. 1998


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


722 A.2d 1129; 1999 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 14


September 14, 1998, Argued  
January 8, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed From No. 95-266 and 268-MG. State Agency, Environmental Hearing Board.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners sought review of the determination of the Environmental Hearing Board (Pennsylvania) which found that respondent, environmental protection department, abused its discretion in allowing petitioner company to renew its permit to operate a municipal waste transfer station.


OVERVIEW: The environmental board determined that respondent, environmental protection department, abused its discretion in allowing petitioner company to renew its permit to operate a municipal waste transfer station. On petitioners', company and township, appeal, the court observed that, assuming that the regulation did apply, petitioner company's permit was clearly voided by 25 Pa. Code § 271.211(e) because no municipal waste was processed or disposed of at the facility within five years of the date that respondent first issued the permit for the facility. Petitioner company contended that the permit gave it a vested right to use real property as a waste transfer station and that this right could not be impaired by government regulation. The court held that because this issue was raised for the first time on appeal, it was waived. The court concluded that respondent's determination that § 271.211(e) did not apply to petitioner's pre-1988 permit was contrary to the plain language of the regulation. Therefore, the board was not required to defer to respondent's interpretation of § 271.211(e).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the board, which determined that respondent, environmental protection department, abused its discretion in allowing petitioner company to renew its permit to operate a municipal waste transfer station. Under Pennsylvania law, the permit lapsed because no municipal waste was processed or disposed of at the facility within five years of the date that the permit was first issued.

 

450 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Kocher v. Bickley


No. 608 M.D. 1998


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


722 A.2d 756; 1999 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 4


October 30, 1998, Submitted On Briefs  
January 5, 1999, Decided  
January 5, 1999, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [**1] The preliminary objections, based on the lack of a clear legal right to relief and no corresponding duty on the Department, are granted and the Petition for Review dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners filed a writ of mandamus seeking to have respondent state issue learner's permits to them without requiring them to supply their social security numbers. Respondent filed objections.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners applied to respondent state for learner's permits with the objective of eventually obtaining driver's licenses. 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 1510(a), 1510(f) require that an applicant must provide his or her social security number or obtain a waiver from the federal government before a license will be issued. The statutes also provide that another identifier may be used, such as a taxpayer identification number. Petitioners did not provide a social security number, waiver, or a taxpayer identification number on religious grounds, and respondent refused to issue them permits. Petitioners requested a mandamus, and respondent objected. The court concluded that social security numbers were unique identifiers that were widely utilized. Social security numbers also provided the most efficient method for locating driver records. The requirement to obtain a waiver or social security number did not impede petitioners from practicing their religious beliefs, as they could forego the privilege to drive. The state had a legitimate interest in monitoring and identifying drivers to ensure that they are competent, qualified and not dangerous to others on its highways.


OUTCOME: The court granted respondent state's objections to petitioners' request for a writ of mandamus. The court held that respondent had a legitimate interest in monitoring and identifying drivers to ensure that they are competent, qualified, and not dangerous to others on respondent's highways.

Paz v. Pennsylvania Hous. Fin. Agency, Homeowners Emergency Mortg. Assistance Loan Program


No. 626 C.D. 1998


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


722 A.2d 762; 1999 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 5


August 21, 1998, Submitted On Briefs  
January 5, 1999, Decided  
January 5, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed From No. Decision dated January 28, 1998. State Agency Pennsylvania Housing Finance Agency.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed a decision from respondent Pennsylvania Housing Finance Agency that denied petitioner state assistance under the Homeowner's Emergency Mortgage Assistance Act because petitioner's mortgage was insured by the Federal Housing Authority under Title II of the National Housing Act, 12 U.S.C.S. §§ 1707-1715z-18.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner's application for state assistance under Homeowner's Emergency Mortgage Assistance Program (HEMAP) was denied on the basis that petitioner's mortgage was insured by the Federal Housing Authority (FHA). Respondent, the Pennsylvania Housing Finance Agency, denied relief to petitioner. On appeal, petitioner claimed that the Homeowner's Emergency Mortgage Assistance Act (State Act), 35 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 1680.401c-1680.410c, which excluded federally protected borrower/mortgagors from its HEMAP assistance programs, violated the federal and state constitutions' equal protection guarantees. The court applied the rational basis level of scrutiny to the classification contained in the State Act. The court stated that petitioner had the burden to show that under no state of facts could the classification further any conceivable legitimate state goal. Petitioner failed to carry this heavy burden. Respondent offered a rational basis for the classification because the classification had the legitimate state goal of conserving funds to provide mortgage assistance for those not otherwise covered by FHA protections. Thus, the State Act passed constitutional muster.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of respondent housing finance agency, which denied state assistance to petitioner, on the grounds that the Homeowner's Emergency Mortgage Assistance Act's exclusion of federally protected borrower/mortgagors from its assistance programs was constitutional.

 

452 of 892 DOCUMENTS


In re Petition to Contest the Primary Election of May 19, 1998


No. 1917 C.D. 1998


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


721 A.2d 1156; 1998 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 910


November 19, 1998, Argued  
December 21, 1998, Decided  
December 21, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed From No. GD 98-9252. Common Pleas Court of the County of Allegheny. Judge McLEAN.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant registered voters challenged the decision of the Common Pleas Court, Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which sustained the preliminary objections, filed by the county elections department and a citizens committee, regarding lack of subject matter jurisdiction, in an action involving the adoption of a home rule charter and an election contest, under the Election Code, 25 P.S. § 3456.


OVERVIEW: The general assembly enacted Act 12, 16 P.S. §§ 6101-C to 6113-C, revising the procedure for a second class county to adopt a home rule charter. Under that legislation, a charter commission drafted a proposed charter that was adopted by a slim margin in a primary election. Seeking to have the adoption of the charter declared unconstitutional and illegal, appellant registered voters filed a petition to contest the primary election, challenging the manner in which Act 12 was enacted and alleging violations of campaign finance law. They did not allege any defect in the conduct of the election. The county elections department and a citizens committee filed preliminary objections by demurrer, requesting a dismissal for lack of subject matter jurisdiction; the trial court sustained the objections. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the Election Code, 25 P.S. § 3456, only allowed challenges based on illegality when the illegality was a violation of those provisions of the Election Code dealing with the conduct of an election. Appellants' challenges did not have anything to do with casting, computation, or return of the vote.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, because election contests could only be brought regarding matters pertaining to the election process itself, such as the conduct of balloting, the tabulation of results, and the return of results. Appellant registered voters did not challenge any aspect of the conduct of the election, thus the trial court properly sustained the preliminary objections and properly dismissed the petition for lack of subject matter jurisdiction.

Purple Orchid v. Pennsylvania State Police, Bureau of Liquor Control Enforcement


No. 440 C.D. 1998


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


721 A.2d 84; 1998 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 887

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended December 7, 1998. As Amended December 14, 1998. Petition for Allowance of Appeal Granted July 28, 1999. Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied August 25, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Pa. LEXIS 2571.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed From. No. 9703-0440. Common Pleas Court of the County of Philadelphia. Judge LEVIN.



DISPOSITION: The order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County at No. 9703-0440, dated December 31, 1997, is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant licensee challenged an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), affirming the decision of the liquor control board which found that appellant permitted improper entertainment on its premises in violation of 47 P.S. § 493(10).


OVERVIEW: Appellant licensee challenged an order of trial court that affirmed a liquor control board finding that appellant permitted improper entertainment on its premises in violation of 47 P.S. § 493(10). Appellant contended that § 493(10) was unconstitutionally vague and violated its rights under U.S. Const. amend. XIV because the improper conduct proscribed by the statute was incapable of being discerned in advance; and violated its freedom of expression rights under U.S. Const. amend. I. The court rejected appellant's argument on the ground that appellant was aware that the board consistently interpreted the statutory provision to mean that nude dancing was prohibited in places where alcohol was sold. The court held that the board's prohibition against nude dancing in licensed liquor establishments did not violate the first amendment as the commonwealth had plenary power to regulate conduct pertaining to liquor sales, the prohibition furthered an important government interest, the prohibition was content neutral and the restriction was no greater than essential. Accordingly the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed because the court determined that appellant's fourteenth amendment rights were not violated as appellant was aware that the board consistently interpreted the statutory provision to mean that nude dancing was prohibited on its premises and the prohibition did not violate appellant's first amendment rights.

Cons. Stat. § 8304(b)(7).


OVERVIEW: Petitioner teacher applied to purchase retirement credit for a maternity leave of absence from respondent Public School Employes' Retirement Board (Pennsylvania). Respondent denied her request as untimely, and appellant sought review. The court reversed, finding that respondent's interpretation of 24 Pa. Cons. OUTCOME: The court reversed respondent Public School Employes' Retirement Board (Pennsylvania)'s denial of petitioner teacher's request to purchase retirement credit for a forced maternity leave of absence, finding that there was a one-year period of eligibility for commencing such a purchase.

Cooper v. Department of Banking


No. 1434 C.D. 1998


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


720 A.2d 832; 1998 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 868


October 9, 1998, Submitted On Briefs  
November 19, 1998, Decided  
November 19, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied March 31, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Pa. LEXIS 910.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed From No. 96-5. State Agency, Department of Banking.



DISPOSITION: The order of the Secretary of Banking is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner committee member sought review of an order in which respondent Department of Banking (Pennsylvania), arguing that respondent was not authorized under the Credit Union Code, 17 Pa. Const. Stat. §503, to remove permanently removed petitioner from his position or to prohibit him from participation in any manner in the affairs of the credit union.


OVERVIEW: A hearing examiner recommended petitioner committee member's permanent removal from the credit committee of a credit union based on findings that petitioner failed to conduct the loan approval process of the committee in accordance with credit union bylaws and failed to observe statutory loan procedures. Thereafter, respondent Department of Banking (Pennsylvania) entered an order permanently removing petitioner from his position on the credit committee and prohibiting him from participation in any manner in the credit union's affairs. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision. Under the Credit Union Code, 17 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 503(a), respondent was granted broad authority to regulate and supervise the credit unions affairs including the authority to order petitioner's removal from a position on the credit committee and to prohibit petitioner from participation in all other affairs of the credit union. Section 503(b), which limited the application of a temporary suspension to directors, officers, and committee members in certain situations, did not limit respondent's authority to prohibit petitioner from participation in the credit union's affairs pursuant to § 503(a).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed respondent Department of Banking's (Pennsylvania) order, concluding that respondent had broad authority that encompassed the authority to permanently remove petitioner committee member from his position and to prohibit him from participation in any manner in the affairs of the credit union.

Starr v. State Bd. of Med.


No. 3146 C.D. 1997


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA

November 4, 1998, Filed

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of an order of the State Board of Medicine (Pennsylvania) revoking his medical license because he had romantic and sexual relations with two of his psychiatric patients, arguing that he had terminated the physician-patient relationships before pursing them socially.


OVERVIEW: Respondent issued an order that revoked petitioner's license to practice medicine because he committed medical malpractice by engaging in immoral, unethical, and unprofessional conduct. Specifically, respondent found that petitioner engaged in romantic and sexual relations with two of his psychiatric patients. Petitioner claimed that he had terminated the physician-patient relationships. It was clear that petitioner attempted to terminate the relationships so that he could pursue his patients socially. The court also held that respondent: (1) applied the correct burden of proof; (2) did not violate petitioner's due process or equal rights; and (3) did not issue a directive, or substantive rule, in violation of the Commonwealth Documents Law.


OUTCOME: The revocation of petitioner's medical license was affirmed because he had romantic and sexual relations with his psychiatric patients. The claim that the doctor-patient relationships had been terminated was unavailing because the romances began during the physician-patient relationships.

J.C. v. Department of Pub. Welfare


No. 1363 C.D. 1998


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


720 A.2d 193; 1998 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 834


September 11, 1998, Submitted on Briefs  
November 4, 1998, Decided  
November 4, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed From No. 01-97-007. State Agency Department of Public Welfare.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner alleged perpetrator of child abuse sought review of an order of respondent Department of Public Welfare (Pennsylvania), which denied his administrative appeal and refused to consider his request to expunge a report listing him as a perpetrator of child abuse, under 23 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 6341(a) of the Child Protective Services Law. Petitioner requested expungement more than seven months after he received notice of the report.


OVERVIEW: Respondent Department of Public Welfare (Pennsylvania) informed petitioner alleged perpetrator of child abuse that a report had been filed against him. More than seven months after this notice, petitioner requested that the report be expunged. Respondent denied his request. Petitioner sought an appeal nunc pro tunc, maintaining that he suffered headaches that prevented him from timely filing an appeal; however, petitioner did not testify at the hearing regarding his illness. Respondent denied the appeal, finding that 23 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 6341(a)(2) of the Child Protective Services Law controlled the timeliness of a request for expungement. Petitioner argued that 23 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 6341(a)(1) allowed him to seek expungement at any time. The court affirmed the order, holding that § 6341(a)(1) controlled, as respondent had discretionary authority to expunge a record so long as the request was filed within 45 days of the period set forth in § 6341(a)(2). Petitioner did not establish entitlement to an appeal nunc pro tunc based on his illness, as he did not testify at the hearing and only indicated that he suffered from the illness at the time of the abuse incident.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order, holding that respondent Department of Public Welfare (Pennsylvania) did not err in denying the request for expungement filed by petitioner alleged perpetrator of child abuse, as he failed to file the request within the 45 day period mandated by the Child Protective Services Law. Petitioner was not entitled to an appeal nunc pro tunc, as he did not establish entitlement based on his alleged illness.

COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA

November 2, 1998, Decided  
November 2, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Weaver v. Pa. Dep't of Corr., 829 A.2d 750, 2003 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 532 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Weaver v. Department of Corrections, 702 A.2d 370, 1997 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 860 (Pa. Commw. Ct., 1997)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent Department of Corrections (Pennsylvania) filed preliminary objections in the nature of a demurrer to petitioner inmate's mandamus and/or prohibition action in which he alleged that respondent's inmate medical service co-pay regulations violated the Regulatory Review Act, 71 P.S. §§ 745.1-745.14, and the Commonwealth Documents Law, 45 P.S. §§ 1102-1602, and that the Medical Services Act, 61 P.S. §§ 1001-1017, was an ex post facto law.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner inmate filed a mandamus and/or prohibition action, alleging that the inmate medical service co-pay regulations promulgated by respondent Department of Corrections (Pennsylvania), pursuant to the Medical Services Act, 61 P.S. §§ 1001-1017, violated the Regulatory Review Act, 71 P.S. §§ 745.1-745.14, and the Commonwealth Documents Law, 45 P.S. §§ 1102-1602. Machipongo Land & Coal Co. v. Department of Envtl. Resources

June 8, 1998, Argued  
September 30, 1998, Decided  
September 30, 1998, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [**1] Motion for summary judgment filed by the Commonwealth denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent commonwealth moved for summary judgment in response to a petition for review by petitioners coal owners challenging a regulation designating portions of their land unsuitable for surface mining.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners coal owners challenged a regulation designating portions of their land unsuitable for mining and requested that the court enjoin enforcement of the regulation as an unconstitutional taking. Respondent commonwealth filed a motion for summary judgment contending that the regulation did not constitute a taking as the unsuitable designation was adopted for a public purpose and did not deprive petitioners of all beneficial use of the land. In order to determine whether a taking occurred the court held that the applicable regulated land standard formula divided the interest in coal taken by the amount of land subject to the regulation. The court held that it was unable to apply the formula as there was no evidence on the record pertaining to the value of the coal estate prior to the unsuitable designation, as to whether the estate had a separate use from the non-regulated portion of the land, or whether all of its economic benefit was lost as a result of the taking. Accordingly summary judgment was denied because genuine issues of material fact remained as to whether a taking occurred.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment was denied because there was no evidence on the record from which the court could determine the interest in coal taken as a result of the regulation or determine the amount of land subject to the regulation in order to determine whether a taking occurred.

September 24, 1998, Decided  
September 24, 1998, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [**1] Preliminary objections sustained and Petition for Review dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents filed preliminary objections to petitioners' request for a declaration that a legislative bill involving public utility regulation was enacted in violation of Pa. Const. art. III, §§ 1, 3.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners challenged Act 138 on the grounds that it was enacted in violation of Pa. Const. art. III, §§ 1, 3. Petitioners sought a declaration from the court that the enactment was thus void. They also sought an order permanently enjoining respondents from taking any action pursuant to Act 138. Respondents filed preliminary objections to the petition for review. The fact that the bill encompassed more than one subject was not a violation of the state constitution.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed with prejudice petitioners request for a ruling that a law was void and could not be applied by respondents, as the procedures surrounding the law's enactment were not violative of the Pennsylvania Constitution.

Naylor v. Township of Hellam


No. 2846 C.D. 1997


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


717 A.2d 629; 1998 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 693


April 14, 1998, Argued  
September 4, 1998, Decided  
September 4, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed From No. 96-SU-04112-08. Common Pleas Court of the County of York. Judge KENNEDY.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant land owners sought review of the Common Pleas Court of the County of York (Pennsylvania) order which, on cross-motions for summary judgment, denied appellants' motion and granted appellee township's motion, contending that the Municipalities Planning Code, 53 P.S. §§ 10101-11202 did not authorize a moratorium ordinance prohibiting certain types of land development while the municipality revised its zoning ordinances.


OVERVIEW: Appellee township enacted an ordinance that imposed a moratorium on new subdivisions and certain land development for a period of one year, while appellee revised its Comprehensive Plan and zoning, subdivision and land development ordinances, thereby preventing continued development from defeating the intended effect of the revised plans and ordinances. The ordinance expired by its own terms in one year. Approximately two weeks before the new plan and ordinances were enacted, appellant land owners submitted preliminary subdivision and development plans to the zoning officer for review. The plans were rejected as they failed to comply with the pending ordinances, and the moratorium was still in effect. The court agreed with the trial court's conclusion that although the power to enact moratoria on subdivision and land development was not expressly authorized by statute, the legislature, through the Pennsylvania Municipalities Planning Code, 53 P.S. §§ 10101-11202, conferred broad authority upon municipalities to regulate land use, and that the power to enact moratoria was incidental to the powers of regulation expressly granted by the code.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order finding the ordinance valid, concluding that the legislature intended to confer broad authority upon municipalities to regulate land use through moratoria on development while land use regulations were being revised, thus ensuring that proposed development would conform to the revised plans and regulations so that health and welfare of the municipality's citizens would be protected and promoted.

DISPOSITION: The State Board of Private Licensed Schools order dated March 6, 1998, at No. 97-4 is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner instructor sought review of a decision from the State Board of Private Licensed Schools (Pennsylvania), that found he had conducted unlicensed activity in violation of the Private Licensed Schools Act, 24 P.S. §§ 6501-6518, and ordered petitioner to cease and desist the activity and to pay a fine.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner instructor advertised and conducted three-week courses in bartender training. The courses were conducted without a license issued by the board of private licensed schools. The court also held that there was no evidence that the board treated petitioner unfairly.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the board of private licensed school's order that found petitioner instructor violated the provisions of the Private Licensed Schools Act for conducting bartending courses without a license because petitioner should have known that a license was required. Murtagh v. County of Berks


NO. 1941 C.D. 1997


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


715 A.2d 548; 1998 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 629


April 15, 1998, Argued  
July 24, 1998, Decided  
July 24, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed From No. 5182-89 A.D. Common Pleas Court of the County of Berks. Judge DAVENPORT, Senior Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought review of an order of the Common Pleas Court of the County of Berks (Pennsylvania), which granted appellees County of Berks and Berks County Board of Assessment Appeals' motion for a judgment on the pleadings in their action challenging real property reassessments and dismissed appellants' complaint seeking monetary damages pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 with prejudice.


OVERVIEW: Appellant taxpayers filed suit against appellees County of Berks and Berks County Board of Assessment Appeals, challenging the policy of reassessing recently purchased properties at fair market value resulting in significantly higher tax assessments than similar neighborhood properties. Appellants sought monetary damages pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The trial court granted appellees' motion for judgment on the pleadings. On review, the court found that the trial court properly dismissed the action as it did not have subject matter jurisdiction over appellants' § 1983 claim as adequate state remedies had not been exhausted. The court found that actions for equitable relief and monetary damages from a state property assessment procedure were barred in the federal courts by comity, equitable restraint, and federal noninterference in state tax actions. The court found the statutory remedies available to appellants were plain, adequate, and complete. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment on the pleadings in favor of appellees County of Berks and Berks County Board of Assessment Appeals as appellant taxpayers did not exhaust adequate state remedies before bringing their claim for monetary damages for violation of their federal rights.

 

464 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Kirk v. Zoning Hearing Bd.


No. 3368 C.D. 1997


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


713 A.2d 1226; 1998 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 555


May 7, 1998, Argued  
July 1, 1998, Decided  
July 1, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied February 19, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Pa. LEXIS 426.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed From No. 97-04104. Common Pleas Court of the County of Chester. Judge GAVIN, President Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order of the Court of Common Pleas of Chester County in the above-captioned matter is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of the order from the Court of Common Pleas of Chester County (Pennsylvania) which affirmed the decision of appellee Zoning Hearing Board denying appellants' challenge to the validity of the minimum lot size requirements under appellee's zoning ordinance for single-family detached dwellings in the agricultural zoning district.


OVERVIEW: Appellants filed an application with appellee zoning board challenging the validity of the minimum lot area requirements for single-family homes permitted in agricultural zoning district. Appellee denied appellants' challenge to the validity of the ordinance. Appellee concluded that the larger minimum lot sizes for single-family homes in the agricultural zoning district than the residential zoning districts served the goal of preserving the prime agricultural land and that such requirements were neither arbitrary nor unreasonable. The lower court affirmed appellee's decision. Appellants again sought review. Appellants argued that appellee had the burden of establishing extraordinary justification to uphold the validity of the ordinance and that appellee failed to meet that burden. The court disagreed and ruled that the extraordinary justification standard was inapplicable to the case. The record supported a conclusion that the ordinance constituted a zoning for density intended to promote the preservation of the prime agricultural land. Hence, the minimum lot size requirement was reasonably related to the legitimate governmental goal of preserving the agricultural land.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the validity of the zoning ordinance which established minimum lot size requirements for single-family detached dwellings in the agricultural zoning district because the record amply supported the conclusion that the ordinance was substantially related to the legitimate goal of preserving the prime farmland and was neither arbitrary nor unduly restrictive as applied to appellants' land.

 

465 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Stewart v. Pennsylvania Bd. of Probation & Parole


No. 908 M.D. 1997


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


714 A.2d 502; 1998 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 539


April 9, 1998, Submitted On Briefs  
June 24, 1998, Decided  
June 24, 1998, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [**1] Respondents' preliminary objection to the lack of original jurisdiction is overruled. The preliminary objection in the nature of a demurrer is sustained and the petition for review is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review in the Commonwealth Court of Pennsylvania, of a decision made by respondents, Department of Corrections and the Pennsylvania Board of Probation and Parole, which denied his request for parole after he served the minimum amount of his sentence. Petitioner sought declaratory and injunctive relief on the basis of violation of his constitutional rights.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner challenged respondents', Department of Corrections and the Pennsylvania Board of Probation and Parole, denial of his parole request, which he made after serving the minimum amount of his sentence. Petitioner contended that the commonwealth had no authority to participate in the Violent Incarceration and Truth-in-Sentencing Incentive Grants Act, 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 13701-712, and that its unauthorized use of the programs denied him due process insofar as it served as an across the board basis for parole denial for violent offenders until they have served at least 85 percent of their prison terms. The court sustained respondents' demurrer. The court held that the commonwealth had an indefinite sentencing plan and could seek qualification for the grants. The court found that because respondents' policy was grounded upon a valid statutorily based reason, it was constitutional for due process purposes. The court held that the policy was not cruel and unusual punishment because there was no right to parole. Finally, the court held that the policy did not violate equal protection principles because it reasonably classified violent offenders, such as petitioner, the same.


OUTCOME: The court sustained respondents', Department of Corrections and the Pennsylvania Board of Probation and Parole, demurrer to petitioner's challenge of his parole denial. The court held that the commonwealth had an indefinite sentencing plan and could seek qualification for the grants. The court also held that respondents' policy did not violate equal protection principles, and did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment.

 

466 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Hagan v. East Pennsboro Twp.


NO. 1920 C.D. 1997, NO. 2088 C.D. 1997


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


713 A.2d 1187; 1998 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 478


April 13, 1998, Argued  
June 11, 1998, Decided  
June 11, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed From No. 2515 Civil 1986. Common Pleas Court of the County of Cumberland. Judge HOFFER.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant township sought review of an order of the Common Pleas Court of Cumberland County (Pennsylvania), which awarded delay damages, interest, and attorney's fees to appellee property owners for appellant's taking of appellee's property.


OVERVIEW: Appellant township proposed to extent sewer services to the property of appellee property owners and filed a declaration of taking. On its easement, appellant raised the level of the ground rendering appellee's basement inaccessible, preventing storage, and eliminating their dog kennel. In a hearing more than eight years later, the trial court awarded delay damages and interest. The court held that the trial court properly tolled the delay damages for a 12-month delay caused by the death of appellee's expert witness. The court held that the trial court erred in computing interest based on the prime rate rather than the commercial loan rate during the delay period. The court found that the trial court's award of attorney's fees was proper because a frivolous motion and an improper discover request by appellant were obdurate, dilatory, and vexatious in nature. The court held that appellant failed to show that it was prejudiced by the admission of testimony concerning settlement negotiations or by the admission of audiotapes of the board of view. Therefore, the court remanded for proper determination of interest and otherwise affirmed the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's computation of interest awarded to appellee property owners in their action based on a taking of their property by appellant township. The court otherwise affirmed the trial court's award of delay damages, interest, and attorney's fees to appellee.

 

467 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Domiano v. Department of Envtl. Resources


No. 1972 C.D. 1997


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


713 A.2d 713; 1998 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 476


April 16, 1998, Argued  
June 8, 1998, Decided  
June 8, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed From No. 96 - Civ - 2378. Common Pleas Court of the County of Lackawanna. Judge O'MALLEY.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant agency sought review of an order from the Court of Common Pleas of Lackawanna County (Pennsylvania) that denied appellant's preliminary objections to respondent individual's petition for appointment of a board of viewers pursuant to Eminent Domain Code § 502, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 26, § 1-502.


OVERVIEW: On July 22, 1993, appellant agency issued a letter to respondent individual, giving official notice of appellant's intention to enter land in which respondent held a leasehold interest for the purpose of accomplishing a stream channel restoration project at an abandoned mine site. Respondent then filed a petition for appointment of board of viewers pursuant to Eminent Domain Code § 502, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 26, § 1-502. Appellant filed preliminary objections in response. Subsequently, the trial court held respondent sufficiently pleaded a de facto taking. The trial court also determined, while respondent provided sufficient facts establishing a right to relief, it was premature to dismiss the case for lack of subject matter jurisdiction. Appellant then sought review. On review, the court reversed and remanded with instructions for transfer to the environmental hearing board, because appellant's preliminary objections made out a claim on their face that appellant acted, not under its eminent domain powers, but under its police powers, and thus, jurisdiction lay with the environmental hearing board.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that denied appellant agency's objections, and remanded with instructions for transfer of respondent individual's petition, because appellant acted pursuant to its police power, not its eminent domain powers, and thus, primary jurisdiction over respondent's petition rested with an administrative hearing board.

 

468 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Myers v. Ridge


No. 542 M.D. 1997


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


712 A.2d 791; 1998 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 334


November 21, 1997, Submitted on Briefs  
May 15, 1998, Decided  
May 15, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied August 2, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Pa. LEXIS 2258.



DISPOSITION:  [**1] The preliminary objections in the nature of a demurrer filed by Respondents to Myers' petition for review are sustained. Myers' petition for review is dismissed with prejudice.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner challenged the decision from respondent Pennsylvania Board of Probation and Parole, which denied his application for parole. Petitioner sought review in the nature of a mandamus requesting relief in the form of a declaratory judgment, injunctive relief, and equitable relief.


OVERVIEW: After respondent Pennsylvania Board of Probation and Parole (Board) denied petitioner's application for parole, he contended that the denial violated his due process and equal protection rights, and that the addition of § 34.1, 61 P.S. § 331.34a(b) (1995), to the Parole Act violated the constitutional prohibition against passage of an ex post facto law. The court sustained the demurrer filed by respondents, Governor, Board, and Pennsylvania Department of Corrections. The court held that there was no due process violation because participation in a community corrections center was not a protected liberty interest. The court also held that there was no ex post facto law violation because there was no constitutional guarantee against change in the law relating to parole. The court concluded that petitioner's contentions that respondent board denied him a fair parole hearing by retroactively applying § 34.1(a)(3) were without merit. Finally, the court held that there was no equal protection violation because the classification and disparate treatment between violent and nonviolent offenders did not offend the concept of due process or equal protection of the law.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the objections filed by respondents, Governor, Pennsylvania Board of Probation and Parole, and Pennsylvania Department of Corrections, to petitioner's parole denial challenge. The court held that there was no due process or equal protection violation, and that there was no violation of the prohibition against passage of ex post facto laws.

 

469 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Kroh v. Unemployment Compensation Bd. of Review


No. 2765 C.D. 1997


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


711 A.2d 1093; 1998 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 335


February 20, 1998, Submitted on Briefs  
May 15, 1998, Decided  
May 15, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied February 10, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Pa. LEXIS 332.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed From No. B-364205. State Agency, Unemployment Compensation Board of Review.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Unemployment Compensation Board of Review is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoner appealed from a decision from respondent Unemployment Compensation Board of Review (Pennsylvania), which held that he was ineligible for unemployment benefits under 43 Pa. Cons. Stat. 802.6 (1996) because he was incarcerated.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner prisoner sought review of a decision of respondent Unemployment Compensation Board of Review which held that he was ineligible for unemployment benefits under 43 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 802.6 (1996), because he was incarcerated. Petitioner argued that denying him benefits violated his rights under the Equal Protection Clause, U.S. Const. XIV. The court stated that because prisoners were not a suspect class there only needed to be a rational reason for the classification to be constitutionally valid. The court held that the General Assembly had a legitimate and rational reason not to want prisoners to receive unemployment benefits because either the prisoners were not sufficiently available for work even though eligible for work release or the denial of benefits was a deterrence of criminal activity. Accordingly, because the statute denying unemployment compensation benefits to incarcerated prisoners was constitutionally valid the court affirmed the decision denying petitioner's benefits.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed respondent Unemployment Compensation Board of Review's denial of benefits to petitioner prisoner because the law denying unemployment compensation benefits to incarcerated prisoners did not violate the equal protection clause since there were rational reasons to deny incarcerated prisoners unemployment compensation benefits.

Indianapolis Power & Light Co. v. Pennsylvania PUC


No. 1597 C.D. 1997


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


711 A.2d 1071; 1998 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 328


December 10, 1997, Argued  
May 7, 1998, Decided  
May 7, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari Denied March 8, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 1739.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed From. No. R-00973877, R-00973877C0001, R-00973877C0002. State Agency, Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission.



DISPOSITION: The order of the Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner power company sought review of the decision from respondent Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission which granted an energy company's application for the issuance of a qualified rate order to recover stranded-costs pursuant to the Electricity Generation Customer Choice and Competition Act, 66 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 2801-12. Petitioner asserted that provisions allowing the recovery of stranded-costs were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner power company provided electricity and was regulated by respondent Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission. Respondent granted an energy company's application for the issuance of a qualified rate order to recover stranded-costs pursuant to the Electricity Generation Customer Choice and Competition Act (the Act), 66 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 2801-12. Petitioner objected to respondent's approval of the application and asserted that the provisions of the Act allowing the recovery of stranded-costs violated the commerce clause of the federal constitution. On review, the court examined the Act referencing the applicable constitutional clauses and principles. The court held that the state's interest in regulating the retail sales of electric utilities, was enough to uphold the stranded-cost provisions under the commerce clause. Further, the court found that the Act did not involve the commerce clause because it promoted competition on equitable terms and the stranded-cost provisions were consistent with traditional state regulation of local electric rates. Therefore, the decision was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The order of respondent Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission was affirmed because the Electricity Generation Customer Choice and Competition Act did not involve the commerce clause. This was because it promoted competition on equitable terms and the stranded-cost provisions were consistent with traditional state regulation of local electric rates.

Topps Chewing Gum v. Workers' Compensation Appeal Bd. (Wickizer)


No. 1996 C.D. 1997


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


710 A.2d 1256; 1998 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 266


February 13, 1998, Argued  
April 23, 1998, Decided  
April 23, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed From. No. A96-3883. State Agency, Workers' Compensation Appeal Board.



DISPOSITION: The order of the Workers' Compensation Appeal Board (WCAB), dated June 30, 1997 at A96-3883, is hereby vacated, and the case is remanded to the WCAB to remand to the workers' compensation judge for a determination of the Petitions for Review of Utilization Review Determination, filed on or about June 6, 1995 and July 28, 1995 by Leroy Pelicci, M.D., placing the burden of proof on the employer, Topps Chewing Gum. Jurisdiction relinquished.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer challenged an order of respondent Workers' Compensation Appeal Board (Pennsylvania), which reversed the dismissal of a claimant's petition by the workers' compensation judge pursuant to the Act 44 amendments to the Workers' Compensation Act.


OVERVIEW: Appellant employer filed petitions for utilization review pursuant to § 306(f.1)(6) of the Act 44 amendments to the Workers' Compensation Act, 77 P.S. § 531(6)(1996), challenging the medical treatment of an employee as unreasonable and unnecessary. After the utilization review organizations (URO) found the medical treatments to be unnecessary, the physician for the employee filed petitions for review of the UROs' findings. A workers' compensation judge (WCJ) found that the employee failed to meet her burden of proof as to the reasonableness of the medical treatment. Respondent Workers' Compensation Appeal Board (board) reversed, finding that the employer had the burden of proof. The court held that the Act 44 amendments placed the burden on the employer but vacated the board's order and remanded to the board for a further remand to the WCJ.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the order of respondent Workers' Compensation Appeal Board (board) and remanded to the board for a further remand to the workers' compensation judge as fact finder to place the burden of proof on the employer with respect to the reasonableness of the employee's medical treatment.
